**Montevideo** ([/ˌmɒntɪvɪˈdeɪoʊ/](/wiki/Help:IPA/English "Help:IPA/English"),^[\[10\]](#cite_note-10)^ [US](/wiki/American_English "American English") also [/-ˈvɪdioʊ/](/wiki/Help:IPA/English "Help:IPA/English");^[\[11\]](#cite_note-11)^
Spanish: [\[monteβiˈðeo\]](/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish "Help:IPA/Spanish")) is the [capital](/wiki/Capital_city "Capital city") and [largest city](/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Uruguay "List of cities in Uruguay") of [Uruguay](/wiki/Uruguay "Uruguay"). According to the 2023 census, the [city proper](/wiki/City_proper "City proper") has a population of 1,302,954 (about 37.2% of the country's total population)^[\[12\]](#cite_note-INEpop-12)^ in an area of 201 square kilometers (78 sq mi). Montevideo is situated on the southern coast of the country, on the northeastern bank of the [Río de la Plata](/wiki/R%C3%ADo_de_la_Plata "Río de la Plata").{#cite_ref-INEpop_12-0}

A Portuguese garrison was established in the place where today is the city of Montevideo in November 1723. The Portuguese garrison was expelled in February 1724 by a Spanish soldier, [Bruno Mauricio de Zabala](/wiki/Bruno_Mauricio_de_Zabala "Bruno Mauricio de Zabala"), as a strategic move amidst the [Spanish](/wiki/Spanish_people "Spanish people")-[Portuguese](/wiki/Portuguese_people "Portuguese people") dispute over the [platine region](/wiki/R%C3%ADo_de_la_Plata_Basin "Río de la Plata Basin"). There is no official document establishing the foundation of the city, but the "Diario" of Bruno Mauricio de Zabala officially mentions the date of 24 December 1726 as the foundation, corroborated by presential witnesses. The complete independence from Buenos Aires as a real city was not reached until 1 January 1730. It was also under brief [British rule in 1807](/wiki/British_invasions_of_the_R%C3%ADo_de_la_Plata "British invasions of the Río de la Plata"), but eventually the city was retaken by Spanish [criollos](/wiki/Criollos "Criollos") who defeated the [British invasions of the River Plate](/wiki/British_invasions_of_the_River_Plate "British invasions of the River Plate"). Montevideo is the seat of the administrative headquarters of [Mercosur](/wiki/Mercosur "Mercosur") and [ALADI](/wiki/ALADI "ALADI"), [Latin America](/wiki/Latin_America "Latin America")'s leading trade blocs, a position that entailed comparisons to the role of [Brussels](/wiki/Brussels "Brussels") in Europe.^[\[13\]](#cite_note-:0-13)^{#cite_ref-:0_13-0}

The 2019 Mercer's report on quality of life, rated Montevideo first in Latin America,^[\[14\]](#cite_note-2019_Quality_of_Living_Survey-14)^ a rank the city has consistently held since 2005.^[\[15\]](#cite_note-Globalization-15)^^[\[16\]](#cite_note-globalizacion.org-16)^^[\[17\]](#cite_note-historico.elpais.com.uy-17)^^[\[18\]](#cite_note-fastcoexist.com-18)^^[\[19\]](#cite_note-mercer.com-19)^ As of 2010^[\[update\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit)^, Montevideo was the 19th largest city economy in [the continent](/wiki/Latin_America "Latin America") and 9th highest income earner among [major cities](/wiki/List_of_Latin_American_cities_by_population "List of Latin American cities by population").^[\[20\]](#cite_note-mckinsey.com-20)^ In 2022, it has a projected [GDP](/wiki/GDP "GDP") of $53.9 billion, with a [per capita](/wiki/GDP_per_capita "GDP per capita") of $30,148.^[\[21\]](#cite_note-ReferenceA-21)^{#cite_ref-ReferenceA_21-0}

In 2018, it was classified as a beta [global city](/wiki/Globalization_and_World_Cities_Research_Network "Globalization and World Cities Research Network") ranking eighth in [Latin America](/wiki/Latin_America "Latin America") and 84th in the world.^[\[22\]](#cite_note-22)^ Montevideo hosted every match during the [first FIFA World Cup](/wiki/1930_FIFA_World_Cup "1930 FIFA World Cup"), in 1930. Described as a "vibrant, eclectic place with a rich cultural life",^[\[23\]](#cite_note-:1-23)^ and "a thriving tech center and entrepreneurial culture",^[\[18\]](#cite_note-fastcoexist.com-18)^ Montevideo ranked eighth in Latin America on the 2013 [MasterCard](/wiki/MasterCard "MasterCard") Global Destination Cities Index.^[\[24\]](#cite_note-24)^{#cite_ref-24}

The city has preserved European architecture,^[\[25\]](#cite_note-25)^ being considered one of the cities with the most [art deco](/wiki/Art_Deco "Art Deco") influence.^[\[26\]](#cite_note-26)^ It is the hub of commerce and higher education in Uruguay as well as its chief port. The city is also the [financial hub](/wiki/Financial_centre "Financial centre") of Uruguay and the cultural anchor of a [metropolitan area](/wiki/Montevideo_metropolitan_area "Montevideo metropolitan area") with a population of around 2 million.{#cite_ref-26}  

Etymology {#Etymology}
----------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit&section=1 "Edit section: Etymology")\]

There are several explanations for the word *Montevideo* . All agree that "Monte" refers to the [Cerro de Montevideo](/wiki/Fortaleza_del_Cerro "Fortaleza del Cerro"), the hill situated across the [Bay of Montevideo](/wiki/Bay_of_Montevideo "Bay of Montevideo"), but there is disagreement about the etymological origin of the "video" part.^[\[27\]](#cite_note-27)^{#cite_ref-27}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Cerro_de_Montevideo_desde_la_ciudad._A%C3%B1o_1865.jpg/250px-Cerro_de_Montevideo_desde_la_ciudad._A%C3%B1o_1865.jpg)](/wiki/File:Cerro_de_Montevideo_desde_la_ciudad._A%C3%B1o_1865.jpg) Cerro de Montevideo as seen from the city, in 1865.

* **Monte vide eu** ("I saw a mount") is the most widespread belief^[\[28\]](#cite_note-OriMon-28)^^[\[29\]](#cite_note-Paisaje_urbano-29)^ but is rejected by the majority of experts, who consider it unlikely because it involves a mix of dialects. The name would come from a [Portuguese](/wiki/Portuguese_language "Portuguese language") expression which means "I saw a mount", wrongly pronounced by an anonymous sailor belonging to the expedition of [Fernando de Magallanes](/wiki/Ferdinand_Magellan "Ferdinand Magellan") on catching sight of the Cerro de Montevideo.{#cite_ref-Paisaje_urbano_29-0}
* **Montem vídeo** ("I see a hill"): This version, a variant of the previous one, suggests that the name comes directly from Latin, stemming from the spontaneous expression of a learned member of Magellan's expedition, who, upon spotting the Cerro de Montevideo, exclaimed: *Montem vídeo* ("I see a hill"). The rest of the crew, who did not speak Latin, mistakenly registered this as the name of the hill they had just sighted, *Monte Vídeo* . This theory is supported by numerous maps and documents from the colonial period that refer to the Cerro de Montevideo with the name *Monte Vídeo.* ^[\[30\]](#cite_note-30)^{#cite_ref-30}
* **Monte Vidi:** This hypothesis comes from the "Diario de Navegación" (Navigational Calendar) of boatswain Francisco de Albo, member of the expedition of [Fernando de Magallanes](/wiki/Ferdinand_Magellan "Ferdinand Magellan"),^[\[28\]](#cite_note-OriMon-28)^ who wrote, "Tuesday of the said \[month of January 1520\] we were on the straits of Cape Santa María \[now [Punta del Este](/wiki/Punta_del_Este "Punta del Este")\], from where the coast runs east to west, and the terrain is sandy, and at the right of the cape there is a mountain like a hat to which we gave the name "Montevidi"."^[\[31\]](#cite_note-de_Navarrete_1825_p._290-31)^ This is the oldest Spanish document that mentions the promontory with a name similar to the one that designates the city, but it does not contain any mention of the alleged cry "Monte vide eu."{#cite_ref-de_Navarrete_1825_p._290_31-0}
* **Monte-VI-D-E-O** (*Monte **VI** **D** e **E** ste a **O**este* , "Sixth mount from east to west"): According to Rolando Laguarda Trías, professor of history, the Spaniards annotated the geographic location on a map or [Portolan chart](/wiki/Portolan_chart "Portolan chart"), so that the mount/hill is the VI (6th) mount observable on the coast, navigating Río de la Plata from east to west.^[\[32\]](#cite_note-tacuycom-32)^^[\[33\]](#cite_note-33)^^[\[34\]](#cite_note-SextMon-34)^ With the passing of time, these words were unified to "Montevideo". No conclusive evidence has been found to confirm this academic hypothesis, nor can it be asserted with certainty which the other five mounts observable before the Cerro were.{#cite_ref-SextMon_34-0}
* **Monte Ovídio** (*Monte Santo Ovídio* ), a less widespread hypothesis of a religious origin,^[\[28\]](#cite_note-OriMon-28)^ stems from an interpolation in the aforementioned *Diario de Navegación* of Fernando de Albo, where it is asserted "corruptly now called Santo Vidio" when they refer to the hat-like mount which they named Monte Vidi (that is, the Cerro de Montevideo). [Auditus of Braga](/wiki/Auditus_of_Braga "Auditus of Braga") (Spanish: *Ovídio* ) was the third bishop of the Roman city of [Braga](/wiki/Braga "Braga") (now in Portugal) in 95 CE, where he was always revered; a monument to him was erected there in 1505. Given the relationship that the Portuguese had with the discovery and foundation of Montevideo, and despite the fact that this hypothesis, like the previous ones, lacks conclusive documentation, there have been those who linked the name of Santo Ovídio or Vídio (appearing on some maps of the time) with the subsequent derivation of the name "Montevideo" given to the region since the early years of the 16th century.{#cite_ref-OriMon_28-2}

When the [Portuguese](/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Portugal,_Brazil_and_the_Algarves "United Kingdom of Portugal, Brazil and the Algarves") invaded the [Banda Oriental](/wiki/Banda_Oriental "Banda Oriental") and annexed it as the province of [Cisplatina](/wiki/Cisplatina "Cisplatina") until 1831, they called the city *Montevidéu*, and pronounced as
European Portuguese: [\[mõtɨviˈðew\]](/wiki/Help:IPA/Portuguese "Help:IPA/Portuguese").  

History {#History}
------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit&section=2 "Edit section: History")\]

### Early history {#Early_history}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit&section=3 "Edit section: Early history")\]

Between 1680 and 1683, Portugal founded the city of [Colonia do Sacramento](/wiki/Colonia_do_Sacramento "Colonia do Sacramento") in the region across the bay from [Buenos Aires](/wiki/Buenos_Aires "Buenos Aires"). This city met with no resistance from the Spanish until 1723, when they began to place fortifications on the elevations around Montevideo Bay. On 22 November 1723, Field Marshal [Manuel de Freitas da Fonseca](/w/index.php?title=Manuel_de_Freitas_da_Fonseca&action=edit&redlink=1 "Manuel de Freitas da Fonseca (page does not exist)") \[[pt](https://pt.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manuel_de_Freitas_da_Fonseca "pt:Manuel de Freitas da Fonseca")\] of Portugal built the Montevieu fort.
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Los_Primeros_Pobladores_de_Montevideo.png/259px-Los_Primeros_Pobladores_de_Montevideo.png)](/wiki/File:Los_Primeros_Pobladores_de_Montevideo.png) Arrival of the first families from the Canary Islands in 1726.

A Spanish expedition was sent from Buenos Aires, organized by the Spanish governor of that city, Bruno Mauricio de Zabala. On 22 January 1724, the Spanish forced the Portuguese to abandon the location and started populating the city, initially with six families moving in from Buenos Aires and soon thereafter by families arriving from the [Canary Islands](/wiki/Canary_Islands "Canary Islands") who were known as [Guanches](/wiki/Guanches "Guanches") or [Canarians](/wiki/Canarians "Canarians"). There was also one significant early Italian resident by the name of Jorge Burgues.^[\[35\]](#cite_note-35)^{#cite_ref-35}

A census of the city's inhabitants was performed in 1724 and then a plan was drawn delineating the city and designating it as *San Felipe y Santiago de Montevideo* , later shortened to Montevideo. The census counted more than 100 families of [Galician](/wiki/Galician_people "Galician people") and Canary Islands origin, more than 1000 indigenous people, mostly [Guaraní](/wiki/Guarani_people "Guarani people"), as well as some [trafficked slaves](/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade "Atlantic slave trade") of [Bantu origin](/wiki/Bantu_peoples "Bantu peoples").^[\[34\]](#cite_note-SextMon-34)^{#cite_ref-SextMon_34-1}

A few years after its foundation, Montevideo became the main city of the region north of the Río de la Plata and east of the [Uruguay River](/wiki/Uruguay_River "Uruguay River"), competing with Buenos Aires for dominance in maritime commerce. The importance of Montevideo as the main port of the Viceroyalty of the Río de la Plata brought it in confrontations with the city of Buenos Aires in various occasions, including several times when it was taken over to be used as a base to defend the eastern province of the Viceroyalty from Portuguese incursions.^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^

In 1776, Spain made Montevideo its main naval base (*Real Apostadero de Marina* ) for the South Atlantic, with authority over the Argentine coast, [Fernando Po](/wiki/Bioko "Bioko"), and the [Falklands](/wiki/Falkland_Islands "Falkland Islands").^[\[36\]](#cite_note-36)^{#cite_ref-36}

Until the end of the 18th century, Montevideo remained a fortified area, today known as [Ciudad Vieja](/wiki/Ciudad_Vieja,_Montevideo "Ciudad Vieja, Montevideo").  

### 19th century {#19th_century}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit&section=4 "Edit section: 19th century")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Monte_Video_from_the_Anchorage_outside_the_Harbour.png/480px-Monte_Video_from_the_Anchorage_outside_the_Harbour.png)](/wiki/File:Monte_Video_from_the_Anchorage_outside_the_Harbour.png) "Monte Video from the Anchorage outside the Harbour" by [Emeric Essex Vidal](/wiki/Emeric_Essex_Vidal "Emeric Essex Vidal") (1820). The earliest securely dated picture of the city.^[\[37\]](#cite_note-37)^

On 3 February 1807, British troops under the command of General [Samuel Auchmuty](/wiki/Samuel_Auchmuty_(British_Army_officer) "Samuel Auchmuty (British Army officer)") and Admiral [Charles Stirling](/wiki/Charles_Stirling "Charles Stirling") occupied the city during the [Battle of Montevideo (1807)](/wiki/Battle_of_Montevideo_(1807) "Battle of Montevideo (1807)"), but it was recaptured by the Spanish in the same year on 2 September when [John Whitelocke](/wiki/John_Whitelocke "John Whitelocke") was forced to surrender to troops formed by forces of the [Banda Oriental](/wiki/Banda_Oriental "Banda Oriental")---roughly the same area as modern Uruguay---and of Buenos Aires.^[\[38\]](#cite_note-38)^ After this conflict, the governor of Montevideo [Francisco Javier de Elío](/wiki/Francisco_Javier_de_El%C3%ADo "Francisco Javier de Elío") opposed the new viceroy [Santiago de Liniers](/wiki/Santiago_de_Liniers "Santiago de Liniers"), and created a government Junta when the [Peninsular War](/wiki/Peninsular_War "Peninsular War") started in Spain, in defiance of Liniers. Elío disestablished the Junta when Liniers was replaced by [Baltasar Hidalgo de Cisneros](/wiki/Baltasar_Hidalgo_de_Cisneros "Baltasar Hidalgo de Cisneros").{#cite_ref-38}

During the [May Revolution](/wiki/May_Revolution "May Revolution") of 1810 and the subsequent uprising of the provinces of Rio de la Plata, the Spanish colonial government moved to Montevideo. During that year and the next, Uruguayan revolutionary [José Gervasio Artigas](/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Gervasio_Artigas "José Gervasio Artigas") united with others from Buenos Aires against Spain.^[\[39\]](#cite_note-Historia-39)^ In 1811, the forces deployed by the [Junta Grande](/wiki/Junta_Grande "Junta Grande") of Buenos Aires and the [gaucho](/wiki/Gaucho "Gaucho") forces led by Artigas started a [siege of Montevideo](/wiki/Siege_of_Montevideo_(1811) "Siege of Montevideo (1811)"), which had refused to obey the directives of the new authorities of the May Revolution. The siege was lifted at the end of that year, when the military situation started deteriorating in the [Upper Peru](/wiki/Upper_Peru "Upper Peru") region.{#cite_ref-Historia_39-0}

The Spanish governor was expelled in 1814. In 1816, Portugal invaded the recently liberated territory and in 1821, it was annexed to the Banda Oriental of Brazil. It was named [Imperial City](/w/index.php?title=Imperial_Cidade&action=edit&redlink=1 "Imperial Cidade (page does not exist)") \[[pt](https://pt.wikipedia.org/wiki/Imperial_Cidade "pt:Imperial Cidade")\] by [Emperor](/wiki/Emperor_of_Brazil "Emperor of Brazil") [Pedro I](/wiki/Pedro_I_of_Brazil "Pedro I of Brazil") when the city was part of the [Empire of Brazil](/wiki/Empire_of_Brazil "Empire of Brazil") as the capital of the [Cisplatina province](/wiki/Cisplatina "Cisplatina").^[\[39\]](#cite_note-Historia-39)^ [Juan Antonio Lavalleja](/wiki/Juan_Antonio_Lavalleja "Juan Antonio Lavalleja") and his band called the *Treinta y Tres Orientales* ("[Thirty-Three Orientals](/wiki/Thirty-Three_Orientals "Thirty-Three Orientals")") re-established the independence of the region in 1825. Uruguay was consolidated as an independent state in 1828, with Montevideo as the nation's capital.^[\[29\]](#cite_note-Paisaje_urbano-29)^ In 1829, the demolition of the city's fortifications began and plans were made for an extension beyond the Ciudad Vieja, referred to as the "Ciudad Nueva" ("new city"). Urban expansion, however, moved very slowly because of the events that followed.^[\[40\]](#cite_note-40)^{#cite_ref-40}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/PlanoMontevideoSitioGrande.JPG/220px-PlanoMontevideoSitioGrande.JPG)](/wiki/File:PlanoMontevideoSitioGrande.JPG) Map of Montevideo during the [Guerra Grande](/wiki/Uruguayan_Civil_War "Uruguayan Civil War") (1843--1851).

Uruguay's 1830s were dominated by the confrontation between [Manuel Oribe](/wiki/Manuel_Oribe "Manuel Oribe") and [Fructuoso Rivera](/wiki/Fructuoso_Rivera "Fructuoso Rivera"), the two revolutionary leaders who had fought against the [Empire of Brazil](/wiki/Empire_of_Brazil "Empire of Brazil") under the command of Lavalleja, each of whom had become the *[caudillo](/wiki/Caudillo "Caudillo")* of their respective faction.^[\[41\]](#cite_note-41)^ Politics were divided between Oribe's *Blancos* ("whites"), represented by the [National Party](/wiki/National_Party_(Uruguay) "National Party (Uruguay)"), and Rivera's *Colorados* ("reds"), represented by the [Colorado Party](/wiki/Colorado_Party_(Uruguay) "Colorado Party (Uruguay)"), with each party's name taken from the color of its emblems. In 1838, Oribe was forced to resign from the presidency; he established a rebel army and began a long civil war, the [Guerra Grande](/wiki/Uruguayan_Civil_War "Uruguayan Civil War"), which lasted until 1851.{#cite_ref-41}

The city of Montevideo suffered a [siege of eight years between 1843 and 1851](/wiki/Great_Siege_of_Montevideo "Great Siege of Montevideo"), during which it was supplied by sea with British and French support.^[\[32\]](#cite_note-tacuycom-32)^ By 1843 Montevideo's population of thirty thousand inhabitants was highly cosmopolitan with Uruguayans making up only a third of it.^[\[42\]](#cite_note-Etche17-42)^ The remaining were chiefly Italian (4205), Spanish (3406), Argentine (2553), Portuguese (659), English (606) and Brazilians (492).^[\[42\]](#cite_note-Etche17-42)^ Oribe, with the support of the then conservative [Governor of Buenos Aires Province](/wiki/Governor_of_Buenos_Aires_Province "Governor of Buenos Aires Province") [Juan Manuel de Rosas](/wiki/Juan_Manuel_de_Rosas "Juan Manuel de Rosas"), besieged the Colorados in Montevideo, where the latter were supported by the French Legion, the Italian Legion, the Basque Legion and battalions from Brazil. Finally in 1851, with the additional support of Argentine rebels who opposed Rosas, the Colorados defeated Oribe.^[\[39\]](#cite_note-Historia-39)^ The fighting however resumed in 1855, when the Blancos came to power, which they maintained until 1865. Thereafter, the Colorado Party regained power, which they retained until the middle of the 20th century.{#cite_ref-Historia_39-2}

After the end of hostilities, a period of growth and expansion started for the city. In 1853 a [stagecoach](/wiki/Stagecoach "Stagecoach") bus line was established joining Montevideo with the newly formed settlement of [Unión](/wiki/Uni%C3%B3n,_Montevideo "Unión, Montevideo") and the first natural gas [street lights](/wiki/Street_light "Street light") were inaugurated.^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^ From 1854 to 1861 the first public sanitation facilities were constructed. In 1856 the Teatro Solís was inaugurated, 15 years after the beginning of its construction. By Decree, in December 1861 the areas of [Aguada](/wiki/Aguada,_Montevideo "Aguada, Montevideo") and [Cordón](/wiki/Cord%C3%B3n "Cordón") were incorporated to the growing *Ciudad Nueva* (New City).^[\[43\]](#cite_note-stats-43)^ In 1866, an underwater telegraph line connected the city with Buenos Aires. The statue of Peace, *La Paz* , was erected on a column in Plaza Cagancha and the building of the Postal Service as well as the bridge of Paso Molino were inaugurated in 1867.^[\[44\]](#cite_note-cronologia-44)^{#cite_ref-cronologia_44-0}

In 1868, the [horse-drawn tram](/wiki/Horsecar "Horsecar") company *Compañía de Tranvías al Paso del Molino y Cerro* created the first lines connecting Montevideo with Unión, the beach resort of [Capurro](/wiki/Capurro "Capurro") and the industrialized and economically independent [Villa del Cerro](/wiki/Villa_del_Cerro "Villa del Cerro"), at the time called *Cosmopolis* . In the same year, the Mercado del Puerto was inaugurated. In 1869, the first railway line of the company *Ferrocarril Central del Uruguay* was inaugurated connecting [Bella Vista](/wiki/Bella_Vista,_Montevideo "Bella Vista, Montevideo") with the town of [Las Piedras](/wiki/Las_Piedras,_Uruguay "Las Piedras, Uruguay"). During the same year and the next, the neighborhoods [Colón](/wiki/Col%C3%B3n_Sudeste "Colón Sudeste"), [Nuevo París](/wiki/Nuevo_Par%C3%ADs "Nuevo París") and [La Comercial](/wiki/La_Comercial "La Comercial") were founded. The Sunday market of Tristán Narvaja Street was established in [Cordón](/wiki/Cord%C3%B3n "Cordón") in 1870. Public water supply was established in 1871. In 1878, *Bulevar Circunvalación* was constructed, a boulevard starting from [Punta Carretas](/wiki/Punta_Carretas "Punta Carretas"), going up to the north end of the city and then turning west to end at the beach of Capurro. It was renamed [Artigas Boulevard](/wiki/Artigas_Boulevard "Artigas Boulevard") in 1885.^[\[44\]](#cite_note-cronologia-44)^ By Decree, on 8 January 1881, the area *Los Pocitos* was incorporated into the *Novísima Ciudad* (Most New City).^[\[43\]](#cite_note-stats-43)^{#cite_ref-stats_43-1}

The first telephone lines were installed in 1882 and electric street lights took the place of the gas-operated ones in 1886. The Hipódromo de Maroñas started operating in 1888, and the neighborhoods of Reus del Sur, [Reus del Norte](/wiki/Reus_al_Norte "Reus al Norte") and [Conciliación](/wiki/Conciliaci%C3%B3n "Conciliación") were inaugurated in 1889. The new building of the School of Arts and Trades, as well as Zabala Square in Ciudad Vieja were inaugurated in 1890, followed by the Italian Hospital in 1891. In the same year, the village of [Peñarol](/wiki/Pe%C3%B1arol,_Montevideo "Peñarol, Montevideo") was founded. Other neighborhoods that were founded were Belgrano and [Belvedere](/wiki/Belvedere,_Montevideo "Belvedere, Montevideo") in 1892, [Jacinto Vera](/wiki/Jacinto_Vera,_Montevideo "Jacinto Vera, Montevideo") in 1895 and Trouville in 1897. In 1894 the new port was constructed, and in 1897, the [Central Railway Station of Montevideo](/wiki/Estaci%C3%B3n_Central_General_Artigas "Estación Central General Artigas") was inaugurated.^[\[32\]](#cite_note-tacuycom-32)^^[\[44\]](#cite_note-cronologia-44)^{#cite_ref-cronologia_44-2}  

### 20th century {#20th_century}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit&section=5 "Edit section: 20th century")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/MontevideoIndependencePlaza1900.jpg/220px-MontevideoIndependencePlaza1900.jpg)](/wiki/File:MontevideoIndependencePlaza1900.jpg) Plaza Independencia around 1900.

In the early 20th century, many Europeans (particularly Spaniards and Italians but also thousands from Central Europe) immigrated to the city. In 1908, 30% of the city's population of 300,000 was foreign-born. In that decade the city expanded quickly: new neighborhoods were created and many separate settlements were annexed to the city, among which were the [Villa del Cerro](/wiki/Villa_del_Cerro "Villa del Cerro"), [Pocitos](/wiki/Pocitos "Pocitos"), the [Prado](/wiki/Prado,_Montevideo "Prado, Montevideo") and [Villa Colón](/wiki/Col%C3%B3n_Sudeste "Colón Sudeste"). The [Rodó Park](/wiki/Parque_Rod%C3%B3 "Parque Rodó") and the [Estadio Gran Parque Central](/wiki/Estadio_Gran_Parque_Central "Estadio Gran Parque Central") were also established, which served as *poles* of urban development.^[\[45\]](#cite_note-45)^{#cite_ref-45}

During the early 20th century, Uruguay saw huge social changes with repercussions primarily in urban areas. Among these changes were the right to divorce (1907) and [women's right to vote](/wiki/Women%27s_suffrage "Women's suffrage").^[\[46\]](#cite_note-46)^{#cite_ref-46}

The 1910s saw the construction of Montevideo's [Rambla](/wiki/Rambla_of_Montevideo "Rambla of Montevideo"); strikes by tram workers, bakers and port workers; the inauguration of electric trams; the creation of the [Municipal Intendencias](/wiki/Intendencia#Uruguay "Intendencia"); and the inauguration of the new port.^[\[47\]](#cite_note-HD1900-47)^{#cite_ref-HD1900_47-0}

In 1913, the city limits were extended around the entire gulf. The previously independent localities of the [Villa del Cerro](/wiki/Villa_del_Cerro "Villa del Cerro") and [La Teja](/wiki/La_Teja "La Teja") were annexed to Montevideo, becoming two of its neighborhoods.^[\[48\]](#cite_note-PieGau-48)^{#cite_ref-PieGau_48-0}

During the 1920s, the equestrian statue of Artigas was installed in [Plaza Independencia](/wiki/Plaza_Independencia "Plaza Independencia"); the [Palacio Legislativo](/wiki/Palacio_Legislativo_(Uruguay) "Palacio Legislativo (Uruguay)") was built; the Spanish [Plus Ultra](/wiki/Plus_Ultra_(flying_boat) "Plus Ultra (flying boat)") flying boat arrived (the first airplane to fly from Spain to Latin America, 1926); prominent politician and former president [José Batlle y Ordóñez](/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Batlle_y_Ord%C3%B3%C3%B1ez "José Batlle y Ordóñez") died (1929); and the ground was broken (1929) for the [Estadio Centenario](/wiki/Estadio_Centenario "Estadio Centenario") (completed 1930).^[\[47\]](#cite_note-HD1900-47)^{#cite_ref-HD1900_47-1}  

### World War II {#World_War_II}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit&section=6 "Edit section: World War II")\]

During World War II, a famous incident involving the [German cruiser *Admiral Graf Spee*](/wiki/German_cruiser_Admiral_Graf_Spee "German cruiser Admiral Graf Spee") took place in [Punta del Este](/wiki/Punta_del_Este "Punta del Este"), 200 kilometers (120 mi) from Montevideo. After the [Battle of the River Plate](/wiki/Battle_of_the_River_Plate "Battle of the River Plate") with the [Royal Navy](/wiki/Royal_Navy "Royal Navy") and [Royal New Zealand Navy](/wiki/Royal_New_Zealand_Navy "Royal New Zealand Navy") on 13 December 1939, the *Graf Spee* retreated to Montevideo's port, which was considered neutral at the time. To avoid risking the crew in what he thought would be a losing battle, Captain [Hans Langsdorff](/wiki/Hans_Langsdorff "Hans Langsdorff") [scuttled](/wiki/Scuttling "Scuttling") the ship on 17 December. Langsdorff committed suicide two days later. The eagle figurehead of the *Graf Spee* was salvaged on 10 February 2006.^[\[49\]](#cite_note-49)^^[\[50\]](#cite_note-50)^{#cite_ref-50}  

### Post-war era {#Post-war_era}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit&section=7 "Edit section: Post-war era")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Calle_Washington_en_Ciudad_Vieja%2C_Montevideo%2C_Uruguay.jpg/233px-Calle_Washington_en_Ciudad_Vieja%2C_Montevideo%2C_Uruguay.jpg)](/wiki/File:Calle_Washington_en_Ciudad_Vieja,_Montevideo,_Uruguay.jpg) A street in Montevideo's Ciudad Vieja.

Uruguay began to stagnate economically in the mid-1950s; Montevideo began a decline, later exacerbated by widespread social and political violence beginning in 1968 (including the emergence of the guerrilla [Movimiento de Liberación Nacional-Tupamaros](/wiki/Movimiento_de_Liberaci%C3%B3n_Nacional-Tupamaros "Movimiento de Liberación Nacional-Tupamaros")^[\[47\]](#cite_note-HD1900-47)^) and by the [Civic-military dictatorship of Uruguay (1973-1985)](/wiki/Civic-military_dictatorship_of_Uruguay_(1973-1985) "Civic-military dictatorship of Uruguay (1973-1985)"). There were major problems with supply; the immigration cycle was reversed.{#cite_ref-HD1900_47-2}

From the 1960s to the end of the dictatorship in 1985, around one hundred people died or [disappeared](/wiki/Forced_disappearance "Forced disappearance") because of political violence. In 1974 another hundred Uruguayans also disappeared in Argentina.^[\[51\]](#cite_note-51)^ In 1980, the dictatorship proposed a new constitution. The project was submitted to a [referendum](/wiki/Referendum "Referendum") and rejected in the first polls since 1971, with 58% of the votes against and 42% in favor. The result weakened the military and triggered its fall, allowing the return of democracy.^[\[52\]](#cite_note-52)^{#cite_ref-52}

In the 1980s, Pope [John Paul II](/wiki/John_Paul_II "John Paul II") visited the city twice. In April 1987, as head of state of [Vatican](/wiki/Vatican_City "Vatican City"), he signed a mediation agreement for the conflict of the [Beagle Channel](/wiki/Beagle_Channel "Beagle Channel").^[\[53\]](#cite_note-VisPap-53)^ He also held a large mass in [Tres Cruces](/wiki/Tres_Cruces "Tres Cruces"), declaring the cross located behind the altar as a monument. In 1988, he returned to the country, visiting Montevideo, [Florida](/wiki/Florida,_Uruguay "Florida, Uruguay"), [Salto](/wiki/Salto,_Uruguay "Salto, Uruguay") and [Melo](/wiki/Melo,_Uruguay "Melo, Uruguay").^[\[53\]](#cite_note-VisPap-53)^{#cite_ref-VisPap_53-1}  

### 21st century {#21st_century}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit&section=8 "Edit section: 21st century")\]

The [2002 Uruguay banking crisis](/wiki/2002_Uruguay_banking_crisis "2002 Uruguay banking crisis") affected several industries of Montevideo. In 2017, the city has maintained 15 years of economic growth, with a [GDP](/wiki/GDP "GDP") of $44 billion, and a [GDP per capita](/wiki/GDP_per_capita "GDP per capita") of $25,900.^[\[20\]](#cite_note-mckinsey.com-20)^^[\[21\]](#cite_note-ReferenceA-21)^{#cite_ref-ReferenceA_21-1}

Montevideo has consistently been rated as having the highest quality of life of any city in Latin America:^[\[54\]](#cite_note-fodors.com-54)^ by 2015^[\[55\]](#cite_note-2015_Quality_of_Living_Survey-55)^^[\[56\]](#cite_note-56)^ it held this rank every year during the decade through 2014.^[\[15\]](#cite_note-Globalization-15)^^[\[16\]](#cite_note-globalizacion.org-16)^^[\[17\]](#cite_note-historico.elpais.com.uy-17)^^[\[18\]](#cite_note-fastcoexist.com-18)^^[\[19\]](#cite_note-mercer.com-19)^{#cite_ref-mercer.com_19-1}  

Geography {#Geography}
----------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit&section=9 "Edit section: Geography")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Uruguay_mapa.png/240px-Uruguay_mapa.png)](/wiki/File:Uruguay_mapa.png) Map of Uruguay showing Montevideo on the Atlantic Ocean, between Argentina and Brazil

Montevideo is situated on the north shore of the Río de la Plata, the arm of the Atlantic Ocean that separates the south coast of Uruguay from the north coast of Argentina; Buenos Aires lies 230 kilometers (140 mi) west on the Argentine side. The [Santa Lucía River](/wiki/Santa_Luc%C3%ADa_River "Santa Lucía River") forms a natural border between Montevideo and [San José Department](/wiki/San_Jos%C3%A9_Department "San José Department") to its west. To the city's north and east is [Canelones Department](/wiki/Canelones_Department "Canelones Department"), with the stream of Carrasco forming the eastern natural border. The coastline forming the city's southern border is interspersed with rocky protrusions and sandy beaches.^[\[57\]](#cite_note-57)^ The Bay of Montevideo forms a natural harbor, the nation's largest and one of the largest in the [Southern Cone](/wiki/Southern_Cone "Southern Cone"), and the finest natural port in the region, functioning as a crucial component of the Uruguayan economy and foreign trade. Various streams crisscross the town and empty into the Bay of Montevideo. Its coastline near the emptying rivers are heavily polluted.^[\[58\]](#cite_note-58)^{#cite_ref-58}

The city has an average elevation of 43 meters (141 ft). Its highest elevations are two hills: the [Cerro de Montevideo](/wiki/Cerro_de_Montevideo "Cerro de Montevideo") and the Cerro de la Victoria, with the highest point, the peak of Cerro de Montevideo, crowned by a fortress, the [Fortaleza del Cerro](/wiki/Fortaleza_del_Cerro "Fortaleza del Cerro") at a height of 134 m (440 ft).^[\[59\]](#cite_note-Fortaleza-59)^ Closest cities by road are [Las Piedras](/wiki/Las_Piedras,_Uruguay "Las Piedras, Uruguay") to the north and the so-called [Ciudad de la Costa](/wiki/Ciudad_de_la_Costa "Ciudad de la Costa") (a conglomeration of coastal towns) to the east, both in the range of 20 to 25 km (16 mi) from the city center. The approximate distances to the neighboring department capitals by road are, 90 km (56 mi) to [San Jose de Mayo](/wiki/San_Jose_de_Mayo "San Jose de Mayo") (San Jose Department) and 46 km (29 mi) to Canelones (Canelones Department).{#cite_ref-Fortaleza_59-0}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Atardecer_en_Pocitos%2C_Montevideo%2C_Uruguay.jpg/239px-Atardecer_en_Pocitos%2C_Montevideo%2C_Uruguay.jpg)](/wiki/File:Atardecer_en_Pocitos,_Montevideo,_Uruguay.jpg) Sunset in Montevideo.  

### Climate {#Climate}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit&section=10 "Edit section: Climate")\]

Montevideo has a [Humid subtropical climate](/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate "Humid subtropical climate") ([Köppen](/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification "Köppen climate classification") [Cfa](/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate "Humid subtropical climate")) in a middle latitude, the city experiences the four seasons. It has cool winters (June to August), warm to hot summers (December to February), mild autumns (March to May) and volatile springs (September to November);^[\[60\]](#cite_note-Climate-60)^ The climate is characterized by having mild temperatures, without harsh cold or extreme heat. There are numerous thunderstorms but no tropical cyclones. Rainfall is regular and evenly spread throughout the year, reaching around 950 millimeters (37 in).^[\[61\]](#cite_note-61)^{#cite_ref-61}

Winters are generally cool, wet, windy and overcast. The average temperature during this season is just above 10 °C (50 °F). Daytime temperatures are generally between 10 °C (50 °F) and 18 °C (64 °F), and night lows between 3 °C (37 °F) and 10 °C (50 °F). During this season, there are bursts of icy and relatively dry winds of continental polar air masses, giving an unpleasant chilly feeling to the everyday life of the city, with daytime temperatures around or below 8 °C (46 °F) and possible night frosts. These occur few times during winter, with temperatures generally not falling below −2 °C (28 °F) because of the oceanic influence that moderates the temperature; a few kilometres inland, frosts are more common and colder. On the other hand, even in the middle of winter it's not uncommon to have temperatures above 20 °C (68 °F) for a few days. Rainfall and [sleet](/wiki/Ice_pellets "Ice pellets") are a frequent winter occurrence, but snowfall is extremely rare: flurries have been recorded only four times but with no accumulation, the last one on 13 July 1930 during the inaugural match of the [World Cup](/wiki/1930_FIFA_World_Cup "1930 FIFA World Cup"),^[\[62\]](#cite_note-62)^ (the other three snowfalls were in 1850, 1853 and 1917); the alleged 1980 [Carrasco](/wiki/Carrasco,_Montevideo "Carrasco, Montevideo") snowfall was actually a [hailstorm](/wiki/Hail "Hail").^[\[63\]](#cite_note-63)^{#cite_ref-63}

Summers are warm-hot and humid, with less wind than other seasons. The average temperature in this season is 23 °C (73 °F). Daytime temperatures are usually between 24 °C (75 °F) and 32 °C (90 °F), while night lows between 14 °C (57 °F) and 22 °C (72 °F). During this season, a moderate wind often blows from the sea in the evenings which has a pleasant cooling effect on the city, in contrast to the more severe summer heat of nearby cities like [Buenos Aires](/wiki/Buenos_Aires "Buenos Aires").^[\[60\]](#cite_note-Climate-60)^ Heat waves come with the north winds, which bring humid and hot air masses from the tropical interior of the continent; temperatures can rise above 35 °C (95 °F). These warm periods are usually followed by thunderstorms, generated by cold fronts from the southwest that lowers temperatures considerably. This phenomenon is regional, and can occur several times all year long.{#cite_ref-Climate_60-1}

The autumn in Montevideo is quite pleasant and not so unstable. Daytime temperatures are in general around 20 °C (68 °F) and nights around 10 °C (50 °F). Spring average temperatures are very similar to the autumn, but the weather in that season tends to be more windy and volatile, with more dramatic changes in a short period of time.

Montevideo has an annual average temperature of 16.7 °C (62.1 °F). The lowest recorded temperature is −5.6 °C (21.9 °F) while the highest is 42.8 °C (109.0 °F).^[\[64\]](#cite_note-DNM1-64)^{#cite_ref-DNM1_64-0}  
{#cite_ref-DNM1_64-1}{#cite_ref-Weather_Atlas_68-0}

### Administrative divisions and barrios {#Administrative_divisions_and_barrios}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit&section=11 "Edit section: Administrative divisions and barrios")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Montevideo_Map.png/220px-Montevideo_Map.png)](/wiki/File:Montevideo_Map.png) Map of the *barrios* of Montevideo

As of 2010^[\[update\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit)^, the city of Montevideo has been divided into 8 political municipalities (*Municipios* ), referred to with letters from A to G, including CH, each presided over by a mayor elected by the citizens registered in the constituency. This division, according to the Municipality of Montevideo, "aims to advance political and administrative decentralization in the department of Montevideo, with the aim of deepening the democratic participation of citizens in governance."^[\[69\]](#cite_note-69)^ The head of each *Municipio* is called an *alcalde* or (if female) *alcaldesa* .^[\[70\]](#cite_note-70)^{#cite_ref-70}

Of much greater importance is the division of the city into 62 *barrios* : neighborhoods or wards.^[\[71\]](#cite_note-71)^ Many of the city's *barrios* ---such as [Sayago](/wiki/Sayago,_Montevideo "Sayago, Montevideo"), [Ituzaingó](/wiki/Ituzaing%C3%B3,_Montevideo "Ituzaingó, Montevideo") and [Pocitos](/wiki/Pocitos "Pocitos")---were previously geographically separate settlements, later absorbed by the growth of the city. Others grew up around certain industrial sites, including the [salt-curing](/wiki/Salting_(food) "Salting (food)") works of [Villa del Cerro](/wiki/Villa_del_Cerro "Villa del Cerro") and the [tanneries](/wiki/Tannery_(facility) "Tannery (facility)") in [Nuevo París](/wiki/Nuevo_Par%C3%ADs "Nuevo París"). Each *barrio* has its own identity, geographic location and socio-cultural activities. A neighborhood of great significance is Ciudad Vieja, that was surrounded by a protective wall until 1829. This area contains most important buildings of the colonial era and early decades of independence.{#cite_ref-71}  
1. [Ciudad Vieja](/wiki/Ciudad_Vieja,_Montevideo "Ciudad Vieja, Montevideo")
2. [Centro](/wiki/Centro,_Montevideo "Centro, Montevideo")
