### Landmarks {#Landmarks}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit&section=12 "Edit section: Landmarks")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Pal%C3%A1cio_Salvo_%283767077980%29.jpg/220px-Pal%C3%A1cio_Salvo_%283767077980%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Pal%C3%A1cio_Salvo_(3767077980).jpg) Palacio Salvo. [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Letras_Montevideo_en_Pocitos.jpg/232px-Letras_Montevideo_en_Pocitos.jpg)](/wiki/File:Letras_Montevideo_en_Pocitos.jpg) [Pocitos](/wiki/Pocitos "Pocitos") is the most populous Montevideo neighborhood.

The architecture of Montevideo ranges from [Neoclassical](/wiki/Neoclassicism "Neoclassicism") buildings such as the [Montevideo Metropolitan Cathedral](/wiki/Montevideo_Metropolitan_Cathedral "Montevideo Metropolitan Cathedral") to the late-modern style of the [World Trade Center Montevideo](/wiki/World_Trade_Center_Montevideo "World Trade Center Montevideo") or the 158-meter (518 ft) [ANTEL Telecommunication Tower](/wiki/Antel_Tower "Antel Tower"), the tallest skyscraper in the country. Along with the Telecommunications Tower, the [Palacio Salvo](/wiki/Palacio_Salvo "Palacio Salvo") dominates the skyline of the Bay of Montevideo. The building facades in the Old Town reflect the city's extensive European immigration, displaying the influence of old European architecture. Notable government buildings include the [Legislative Palace](/wiki/Palacio_Legislativo_(Uruguay) "Palacio Legislativo (Uruguay)"), the [City Hall](/wiki/City_Hall_of_Montevideo "City Hall of Montevideo"), [Estévez Palace](/wiki/Est%C3%A9vez_Palace "Estévez Palace") and the [Executive Tower](/wiki/Executive_Tower "Executive Tower"). The most notable sports stadium is the [Estadio Centenario](/wiki/Estadio_Centenario "Estadio Centenario") within [Parque Batlle](/wiki/Parque_Batlle "Parque Batlle"). Parque Batlle, [Parque Rodó](/wiki/Parque_Rod%C3%B3 "Parque Rodó") and [Parque Prado](/wiki/Prado,_Montevideo "Prado, Montevideo") are Montevideo's three great parks.^[\[72\]](#cite_note-72)^{#cite_ref-72}

The [Pocitos](/wiki/Pocitos "Pocitos") district, near the beach of the same name, has many homes built by Bello and Reboratti between 1920 and 1940, with a mixture of styles. Other landmarks in Pocitos are the "[Edificio Panamericano](/wiki/Edificio_Panamericano "Edificio Panamericano")" designed by Raul Sichero,^[\[73\]](#cite_note-73)^ and the "Positano" and "El Pilar" designed by Adolfo Sommer Smith and [Luis García Pardo](/w/index.php?title=Luis_Garc%C3%ADa_Pardo&action=edit&redlink=1 "Luis García Pardo (page does not exist)") \[[es](https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luis_Garc%C3%ADa_Pardo "es:Luis García Pardo")\] in the 1950s and 1960s. However, the construction boom of the 1970s and 1980s transformed the face of this neighborhood, with a cluster of modern apartment buildings for upper and upper middle-class residents.^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^{#cite_ref-73}  

#### Palacio Legislativo {#Palacio_Legislativo}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit&section=13 "Edit section: Palacio Legislativo")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Palacio_Legislativo--.JPG/220px-Palacio_Legislativo--.JPG)](/wiki/File:Palacio_Legislativo--.JPG) The [Legislative Palace](/wiki/Palacio_Legislativo_(Uruguay) "Palacio Legislativo (Uruguay)").

The [Palacio Legislativo](/wiki/Palacio_Legislativo_(Uruguay) "Palacio Legislativo (Uruguay)") in Aguada, north of the city center, is the seat of the [Uruguayan Parliament](/wiki/General_Assembly_of_Uruguay "General Assembly of Uruguay"). Construction started in 1904 and was sponsored by the government of President [José Batlle y Ordóñez](/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Batlle_y_Ord%C3%B3%C3%B1ez "José Batlle y Ordóñez").^[\[74\]](#cite_note-travel-74)^ It was designed by [Italian architects](/wiki/Architecture_of_Italy "Architecture of Italy") [Vittorio Meano](/wiki/Vittorio_Meano "Vittorio Meano") and [Gaetano Moretti](/w/index.php?title=Gaetano_Moretti&action=edit&redlink=1 "Gaetano Moretti (page does not exist)") \[[it](https://it.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gaetano_Moretti "it:Gaetano Moretti")\], who planned the building's interior. Among the notable contributors to the project was sculptor [José Belloni](/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Belloni "José Belloni"), who contributed numerous [reliefs](/wiki/Relief "Relief") and [allegorical sculptures](/wiki/Allegorical_sculpture "Allegorical sculpture").^[\[74\]](#cite_note-travel-74)^{#cite_ref-travel_74-1}  

#### World Trade Center Montevideo {#World_Trade_Center_Montevideo}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit&section=14 "Edit section: World Trade Center Montevideo")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/World_Trade_Center_Montevideo.jpg/220px-World_Trade_Center_Montevideo.jpg)](/wiki/File:World_Trade_Center_Montevideo.jpg) [World Trade Center Montevideo](/wiki/World_Trade_Center_Montevideo "World Trade Center Montevideo").  
Main article: [World Trade Center Montevideo](/wiki/World_Trade_Center_Montevideo "World Trade Center Montevideo")

[World Trade Center Montevideo](/wiki/World_Trade_Center_Montevideo "World Trade Center Montevideo") officially opened in 1998, but work was completed in 2009. The complex is composed of three towers, two three-story buildings called World Trade Center Plaza and World Trade Center Avenue and a large central square called Towers Square. World Trade Center 1 was the first building to be inaugurated, in 1998.^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^ It has 22 floors and 17,100 square meters of space. That same year the avenue and the auditorium were raised. World Trade Center 2 was inaugurated in 2002, a twin tower of World Trade Center 1. Finally, in 2009, World Trade Center 3 and the World Trade Center Plaza and the Towers Square were inaugurated. It is located between the avenues Luis Alberto de Herrera and 26 de Marzo and has 19 floors and 27,000 square meters (290,000 sq ft) of space. The 6,300-square-meter (68,000 sq ft) ^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^ World Trade Center Plaza is designed to be a center of gastronomy opposite Towers Square and Bonavita St.

The Towers Square, is an area of remarkable aesthetic design, intended to be a platform for the development of business activities, art exhibitions, dance and music performances and social places. This square connects the different buildings and towers which comprise the WTC Complex and it is the main access to the complex. The square contains various works of art, notably a sculpture by renowned Uruguayan sculptor [Pablo Atchugarry](/wiki/Pablo_Atchugarry "Pablo Atchugarry"). World Trade Center 4, with 40 floors and 53,500 square meters (576,000 sq ft) of space is under construction as of 2010^[\[update\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit)^.^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^  

#### Telecommunications Tower {#Telecommunications_Tower}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit&section=15 "Edit section: Telecommunications Tower")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Torre_Antel_-_panoramio.jpg/220px-Torre_Antel_-_panoramio.jpg)](/wiki/File:Torre_Antel_-_panoramio.jpg) [Telecommunications Tower](/wiki/Antel_Tower "Antel Tower").  
Main article: [Telecommunications Tower (Montevideo)](/wiki/Telecommunications_Tower_(Montevideo) "Telecommunications Tower (Montevideo)")

Torre de las Telecomunicaciones (Telecommunications Tower) or Torre Antel (Antel Tower) is the 158 meters (518 ft), 37-floor headquarters of Uruguay's [government-owned](/wiki/Government-owned "Government-owned") telecommunications company, [ANTEL](/wiki/ANTEL "ANTEL"), and is the tallest building in the country. It was designed by architect [Carlos Ott](/wiki/Carlos_Ott "Carlos Ott"). It is situated by the side of the Bay of Montevideo. The tower was completed by [American Bridge Company](/wiki/American_Bridge_Company "American Bridge Company") and other design/build consortium team members on 15 March 2000.

When its construction was announced, many politicians complained about its cost (US$40 million, plus US$25 million for the construction of the other 5 buildings of the Telecommunications Complex). Problems during its construction turned the original US$65 million price into US$102 million.  

#### Ciudad Vieja (Old City) {#Ciudad_Vieja_.28Old_City.29}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit&section=16 "Edit section: Ciudad Vieja (Old City)")\]  
Main article: [Ciudad Vieja, Montevideo](/wiki/Ciudad_Vieja,_Montevideo "Ciudad Vieja, Montevideo")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Alcoh%C3%B3licos_An%C3%B3nimos%2C_Montevideo_URU.jpg/220px-Alcoh%C3%B3licos_An%C3%B3nimos%2C_Montevideo_URU.jpg)](/wiki/File:Alcoh%C3%B3licos_An%C3%B3nimos,_Montevideo_URU.jpg) Headquarters of Alcohólicos Anónimos in Montevideo

Ciudad Vieja was the earliest part of the city to be developed and today it constitutes a prominent *[barrio](/wiki/Barrio "Barrio")* of southwest Montevideo. It contains many colonial buildings and national heritage sites, but also many banks, administrative offices, museums, art galleries, cultural institutions, restaurants and nightclubs, making it vibrant with life. Its northern coast is the main port of Uruguay, one of the few deep-draft ports in the Southern Cone of South America.
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/PlazaConstituci%C3%B3n.jpg/220px-PlazaConstituci%C3%B3n.jpg)](/wiki/File:PlazaConstituci%C3%B3n.jpg) Plaza de la Constitución in winter.

Montevideo's most important [plaza](/wiki/Plaza "Plaza") is [Plaza Independencia](/wiki/Plaza_Independencia "Plaza Independencia"), located between Ciudad Vieja and [downtown](/wiki/Centro,_Montevideo "Centro, Montevideo") Montevideo. It starts with the [Gateway of The Citadel](/wiki/Ciudadela,_Montevideo "Ciudadela, Montevideo") at one end and ends at the beginning of [18 de Julio Avenue](/wiki/18_de_Julio_Avenue "18 de Julio Avenue"). It is the remaining part of the wall that surrounded the oldest part of the city.^[\[75\]](#cite_note-75)^ Several notable buildings are located here.{#cite_ref-75}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/TEATRO_SOLIS_01.JPG/220px-TEATRO_SOLIS_01.JPG)](/wiki/File:TEATRO_SOLIS_01.JPG) Solís Theatre.

The [Solís Theatre](/wiki/Sol%C3%ADs_Theatre "Solís Theatre") is Uruguay's oldest theater. It was built in 1856 and is owned by the government of Montevideo. In 1998, the government of Montevideo started a major reconstruction of the theater, which included two US$110,000 columns designed by [Philippe Starck](/wiki/Philippe_Starck "Philippe Starck"). The reconstruction was completed in 2004, and the theater reopened in August of that year.^[\[76\]](#cite_note-76)^ The plaza is also the site of the offices of the [President of Uruguay](/wiki/President_of_Uruguay "President of Uruguay") (both the [Estévez Palace](/wiki/Est%C3%A9vez_Palace "Estévez Palace") and the [Executive Tower](/wiki/Executive_Tower "Executive Tower")). The [Artigas Mausoleum](/wiki/Artigas_Mausoleum "Artigas Mausoleum") is located at the center of the plaza. Statues include that of [José Gervasio Artigas](/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Gervasio_Artigas "José Gervasio Artigas"), a hero of Uruguay's independence movement; an honor guard keeps vigil at the Mausoleum.^[\[77\]](#cite_note-Sights-77)^{#cite_ref-Sights_77-0}

[Palacio Salvo](/wiki/Palacio_Salvo "Palacio Salvo"), at the intersection of 18 de Julio Avenue and Plaza Independencia, was designed by the architect [Mario Palanti](/wiki/Mario_Palanti "Mario Palanti") and completed in 1925. Palanti, an Italian immigrant living in Buenos Aires, used a similar design for his [Palacio Barolo](/wiki/Palacio_Barolo "Palacio Barolo") in Buenos Aires, Argentina. Palacio Salvo stands 100 meters (330 ft) high, including its antenna. It is built on the former site of the Confitería La Giralda, renowned for being where [Gerardo Matos Rodríguez](/wiki/Gerardo_Matos_Rodr%C3%ADguez "Gerardo Matos Rodríguez") wrote his tango "[La Cumparsita](/wiki/La_Cumparsita "La Cumparsita")" (1917.)^[\[78\]](#cite_note-78)^ Palacio Salvo was originally intended to function as a hotel but is now a mixture of offices and private residences.^[\[79\]](#cite_note-79)^{#cite_ref-79}

Also of major note in Ciudad Vieja is the [Plaza de la Constitución](/wiki/Constitution_Square_(Montevideo) "Constitution Square (Montevideo)") (or *Plaza Matriz* ). During the first decades of Uruguayan independence this square was the main hub of city life. On the square are the [Cabildo](/wiki/Cabildo_de_Montevideo "Cabildo de Montevideo")---the seat of colonial government---and the [Montevideo Metropolitan Cathedral](/wiki/Montevideo_Metropolitan_Cathedral "Montevideo Metropolitan Cathedral"). The cathedral is the burial place of [Fructuoso Rivera](/wiki/Fructuoso_Rivera "Fructuoso Rivera"), [Juan Antonio Lavalleja](/wiki/Juan_Antonio_Lavalleja "Juan Antonio Lavalleja") and [Venancio Flores](/wiki/Venancio_Flores "Venancio Flores"). Another notable square is [Plaza Zabala](/wiki/Plaza_Zabala "Plaza Zabala") with the equestrian statue of [Bruno Mauricio de Zabala](/wiki/Bruno_Mauricio_de_Zabala "Bruno Mauricio de Zabala"). On its south side, [Palacio Taranco](/wiki/Palacio_Taranco "Palacio Taranco"), once residence of the Ortiz Taranco brothers, is now the Museum of Decorative Arts. A few blocks northwest of Plaza Zabala is the Mercado del Puerto, another major tourist destination.  

#### Parque Batlle {#Parque_Batlle}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit&section=17 "Edit section: Parque Batlle")\]  
Main article: [Parque Batlle](/wiki/Parque_Batlle "Parque Batlle")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/La_Carreta_y_su_reflejo.JPG/220px-La_Carreta_y_su_reflejo.JPG)](/wiki/File:La_Carreta_y_su_reflejo.JPG) Monumento La Carreta.

Parque Batlle^[\[80\]](#cite_note-Finzer-80)^ (formerly: *Parque de los Aliados* ,^[\[81\]](#cite_note-detubarrio-81)^ translation: "Park of the Allies") is a major public central park, located south of [Avenida Italia](/wiki/Avenida_Italia "Avenida Italia") and north of Avenue Rivera. Along with [Parque Prado](/wiki/Prado,_Montevideo "Prado, Montevideo") and [Parque Rodó](/wiki/Parque_Rod%C3%B3 "Parque Rodó") it is one of three large parks that dominate Montevideo.^[\[82\]](#cite_note-82)^ The park and surrounding area constitute one of the 62 neighborhoods (*barrios* ) of the city. The barrio of Parque Batlle is one of seven coastal barrios, the others being [Buceo](/wiki/Buceo "Buceo"), Carrasco, Malvin, [Pocitos](/wiki/Pocitos "Pocitos"), Punta Carretas, and Punta Gorda.^[\[83\]](#cite_note-Couriel-83)^ The barrio of Parque Battle includes four former districts: Belgrano, Italiano, Villa Dolores and Batlle Park itself and borders the neighborhoods of [La Blanqueada](/wiki/La_Blanqueada "La Blanqueada"), [Tres Cruces](/wiki/Tres_Cruces "Tres Cruces"), Pocitos and Buceo. It has a high population density and most of its households are of medium-high- or high-income.^[\[84\]](#cite_note-84)^ Villa Dolores, a sub-district of Parque Batlle, took its name from the original villa of Don Alejo Rossell y Rius and of Doña Dolores Pereira de Rossel. On their grounds, they started a private collection of animals that became a zoological garden and was passed to the city in 1919;^[\[85\]](#cite_note-montevideo.gub.uy/Zoologico-85)^ in 1955 the [Planetarium of Montevideo](/wiki/Planetario_de_Montevideo "Planetario de Montevideo") was built within its premises.^[\[86\]](#cite_note-montevideo.gub.uy/planetario-86)^{#cite_ref-montevideo.gub.uy/planetario_86-0}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Obelisco_a_los_Constituyentes_de_1830._%281%29.JPG/220px-Obelisco_a_los_Constituyentes_de_1830._%281%29.JPG)](/wiki/File:Obelisco_a_los_Constituyentes_de_1830._(1).JPG) [Obelisk of Montevideo](/wiki/Obelisk_of_Montevideo "Obelisk of Montevideo") in the Parque Batlle.

Parque Batlle is named in honor of [José Batlle y Ordóñez](/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Batlle_y_Ord%C3%B3%C3%B1ez "José Batlle y Ordóñez"), [President of Uruguay](/wiki/President_of_Uruguay "President of Uruguay") from 1911 to 1915.^[\[87\]](#cite_note-montevideogubuy-87)^ The park was originally proposed by an Act of March 1907, which also projected wide boulevards and avenues.^[\[88\]](#cite_note-Parque-88)^^[\[89\]](#cite_note-89)^ French landscape architect, [Carlos Thays](/wiki/Carlos_Thays "Carlos Thays"), began the plantings in 1911. In 1918, the park was named *Parque de los Aliados* , following the victory of the [Allies of World War I](/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_I "Allies of World War I"). On 5 May 1930, after significant expansion, it was again renamed as Parque Batlle y Ordóñez, in memory of the prominent politician and president, who had died in 1929.^[\[88\]](#cite_note-Parque-88)^ The park was designated a National Historic Monument Park in 1975.^[\[87\]](#cite_note-montevideogubuy-87)^^[\[88\]](#cite_note-Parque-88)^ As of 2010^[\[update\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit)^, the park covers an area of 60 hectares (150 acres) and is considered the "lung" of the Montevideo city due to the large variety of trees planted here.^[\[88\]](#cite_note-Parque-88)^^\[*[better source needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS "Wikipedia:NOTRS")*\]^{#cite_ref-Parque_88-3}

The [Estadio Centenario](/wiki/Estadio_Centenario "Estadio Centenario"), the national football stadium, opened in 1930 for the first [World Cup](/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup "FIFA World Cup"), and later hosted several other sporting grounds of note (see *[Sports](#Sports)*).

In 1934, sculptor [José Belloni](/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Belloni "José Belloni")'s "La Carreta", a bronze monument on granite base,^[\[90\]](#cite_note-turismoenuruguaycomuy-90)^ was installed on Avenida Lorenzo Merola near Estadio Centenario. One of several statues in the park, it depicts [yoked](/wiki/Yoke "Yoke") oxen pulling a loaded wagon.^[\[91\]](#cite_note-Box-91)^ It was designated a national monument in 1976.^[\[90\]](#cite_note-turismoenuruguaycomuy-90)^ Another statue on the same side of the park is a bronze copy of the [Discobolus](/wiki/Discobolus "Discobolus") of Myron.{#cite_ref-turismoenuruguaycomuy_90-1}

On the west side of Parque Batlle, on [Artigas Boulevard](/wiki/Artigas_Boulevard "Artigas Boulevard"), the 1938 [Obelisk of Montevideo](/wiki/Obelisk_of_Montevideo "Obelisk of Montevideo") is a monument dedicated to those who created the first Constitution. The work of sculptor [José Luis Zorrilla de San Martín](/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Zorrilla_de_San_Mart%C3%ADn "José Luis Zorrilla de San Martín") (1891--1975), it is a three-sided granite obelisk, 40 meters (130 ft) tall, with bronze statues on its three sides, representing "Law", "Liberty", and "Force", respectively. It has been a National Heritage Site since 1976.^[\[92\]](#cite_note-montevideo.gub.uy-92)^{#cite_ref-montevideo.gub.uy_92-0}  

#### Parque Prado {#Parque_Prado}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit&section=18 "Edit section: Parque Prado")\]  
Main article: [Parque Prado](/wiki/Parque_Prado "Parque Prado")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Puente_sobre_el_arroyo_Miguelete_en_el_Parque_del_Prado.JPG/225px-Puente_sobre_el_arroyo_Miguelete_en_el_Parque_del_Prado.JPG)](/wiki/File:Puente_sobre_el_arroyo_Miguelete_en_el_Parque_del_Prado.JPG) Bridge over the Miguelete stream in the Prado Park.

Established in 1873, the largest of Montevideo's six main public parks is the 1.06-square-kilometre (260-acre) [Parque Prado](/wiki/Parque_Prado "Parque Prado").^[\[93\]](#cite_note-Bulletin27-93)^ Located in the northern part of the city, the Miguelete Creek flows through the park and the neighborhood and of the same name. It is surrounded by the avenues Agraciada, Obes Lucas, Joaquín Suárez, Luis Alberto de Herrera and by the streets Castro and José María Reyes.{#cite_ref-Bulletin27_93-0}

The most frequented areas of the park are the *Rosedal* , a public rose garden with [pergolas](/wiki/Pergola "Pergola"), the Botanical Garden, the area around the Hotel del Prado, as well as the *Rural del Prado* , a seasonal cattle and farm animal fairground. The Rosedal contains four pergolas, eight domes, and a fountain; its 12,000 roses were imported from France in 1910.^[\[94\]](#cite_note-Rosedal-94)^ There are several jogging paths along the Miguelete river.{#cite_ref-Rosedal_94-0}

The Presidential Residence is located behind the Botanical Gardens. Established in 1930, [Juan Manuel Blanes Museum](/wiki/Juan_Manuel_Blanes_Museum "Juan Manuel Blanes Museum") is situated in the [Palladian](/wiki/Palladian_architecture "Palladian architecture") villa, a National Heritage Site since 1975, and includes a Japanese garden.^[\[95\]](#cite_note-MuseoBlanes-95)^ The Professor Atilio Lombardo Museum and Botanical Gardens were established in 1902. The National Institute of Physical Climatology and its observatory are also in the Prado.^[\[96\]](#cite_note-Mesa-96)^{#cite_ref-Mesa_96-0}  

#### Parque Rodó {#Parque_Rod.C3.B3}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit&section=19 "Edit section: Parque Rodó")\]  
Main article: [Parque Rodó](/wiki/Parque_Rod%C3%B3 "Parque Rodó")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/BMR_Parquerodo08%400.jpg/220px-BMR_Parquerodo08%400.jpg)](/wiki/File:BMR_Parquerodo08@0.jpg) Parque Rodó park. [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Carrousel_iluminado.JPG/241px-Carrousel_iluminado.JPG)](/wiki/File:Carrousel_iluminado.JPG) Parque Rodó amusement park.

[Parque Rodó](/wiki/Parque_Rod%C3%B3 "Parque Rodó") is both a *barrio* (neighborhood) of Montevideo and a park which lies mostly outside the limits of the neighborhood itself and belongs to [Punta Carretas](/wiki/Punta_Carretas "Punta Carretas"). The name "Rodó" commemorates José Enrique Rodó, an important Uruguayan writer whose monument is in the southern side of the main park. The park was conceived as a French-style city park.^[\[97\]](#cite_note-Urug_Now-97)^ Apart from the main park area which is delimited by Sarmiento Avenue to the south, Parque Rodó includes an amusement park; the [Estadio Luis Franzini](/wiki/Estadio_Luis_Franzini "Estadio Luis Franzini"), belonging to Defensor Sporting; the front lawn of the Faculty of Engineering and a strip west of the [Club de Golf de Punta Carretas](/wiki/Club_de_Golf_del_Uruguay "Club de Golf del Uruguay") that includes the *Canteras* ("quarry") *del Parque Rodó* , the *Teatro de Verano* ("summer theatre") and the *Lago* ("lake") *del Parque Rodó* .^[\[98\]](#cite_note-Google_maps-98)^{#cite_ref-Google_maps_98-0}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Facultad_de_Ingenier%C3%ADa_ubicada_en_Montevideo.jpg/229px-Facultad_de_Ingenier%C3%ADa_ubicada_en_Montevideo.jpg)](/wiki/File:Facultad_de_Ingenier%C3%ADa_ubicada_en_Montevideo.jpg) Faculty of Engineering located in Parque Rodó.

On the east side of the main park area is the National Museum of Visual Arts. On this side, a street market takes place every Sunday. On the north side is an artificial lake with a little castle housing a municipal library for children. An area to its west is used as an open-air exhibition of photography. West of the park, across the coastal avenue Rambla Presidente Wilson, stretches Ramirez Beach. Directly west of the main park area, and belonging to Parque Rodó *barrio* , there is the former *Parque Hotel* , now called *Edifício Mercosur* , the seat of the parliament of the member countries of the [Mercosur](/wiki/Mercosur "Mercosur").^[\[99\]](#cite_note-ParlMercosur-99)^ During the guerilla war the [Tupamaros](/wiki/Tupamaros "Tupamaros") frequently attacked buildings in this area, including the old hotel.^[\[100\]](#cite_note-100)^{#cite_ref-100}  

#### Forts {#Forts}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit&section=20 "Edit section: Forts")\]

The first set of subsidiary forts was planned by the Portuguese at Montevideo in 1701 to establish a front-line base to stop frequent insurrections by the Spaniards emanating from Buenos Aires. These fortifications were planned within the River Plate estuary at [Colonia del Sacramento](/wiki/Colonia_del_Sacramento "Colonia del Sacramento"). However, this plan came to fruition only in November 1723, when Captain Manuel Henriques de Noronha reached the shores of Montevideo with soldiers, guns and colonists on his warship *Nossa Senhora de Oliveara* . They built a small square fortification. However, under siege from forces from Buenos Aires, the Portuguese withdrew from Montevideo Bay in January 1724, after signing an agreement with the Spaniards.^[\[101\]](#cite_note-Marley-101)^{#cite_ref-Marley_101-0}  

##### Fortaleza del Cerro (Fortress del Cerro) {#Fortaleza_del_Cerro_.28Fortress_del_Cerro.29}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit&section=21 "Edit section: Fortaleza del Cerro (Fortress del Cerro)")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Fortaleza_del_cerro_%28fachada%29.jpg/220px-Fortaleza_del_cerro_%28fachada%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Fortaleza_del_cerro_(fachada).jpg) Fortaleza del Cerro.  
Main article: [Fortaleza del Cerro](/wiki/Fortaleza_del_Cerro "Fortaleza del Cerro")

Fortaleza del Cerro overlooks the bay of Montevideo. An observation post at this location was first built by the Spanish in the late 18th century. In 1802, a beacon replaced the observation post; construction of the fortress began in 1809 and was completed in 1839.^[\[59\]](#cite_note-Fortaleza-59)^ It has been involved in many historical developments and has been repeatedly taken over by various sides. In 1907, the old beacon was replaced with a stronger electric one. It has been a National Monument since 1931^[\[102\]](#cite_note-102)^ and has housed a military museum since 1916.^[\[59\]](#cite_note-Fortaleza-59)^ Today it is one of the tourist attractions of Montevideo.{#cite_ref-Fortaleza_59-2}  

#### Punta Brava Lighthouse {#Punta_Brava_Lighthouse}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit&section=22 "Edit section: Punta Brava Lighthouse")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Faro_Punta_Brava%2C_Montevideo.jpg/220px-Faro_Punta_Brava%2C_Montevideo.jpg)](/wiki/File:Faro_Punta_Brava,_Montevideo.jpg) Punta Brava lighthouse.

[Punta Brava Lighthouse](/wiki/Punta_Brava_Lighthouse "Punta Brava Lighthouse") (*Faro Punta Brava* ), also known as Punta Carretas Lighthouse, was erected in 1876. The lighthouse is 21 meters (69 ft) high and its light reaches 24 km (15 mi) away, with a flash every ten seconds.^[\[103\]](#cite_note-HCV-103)^ In 1962, the lighthouse became electric. The lighthouse is important for guiding boats into the Banco Inglés Buceo Port or the entrance of the Santa Lucía River.{#cite_ref-HCV_103-0}  

#### Rambla of Montevideo {#Rambla_of_Montevideo}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit&section=23 "Edit section: Rambla of Montevideo")\]  
Main article: [Rambla of Montevideo](/wiki/Rambla_of_Montevideo "Rambla of Montevideo")

The **Rambla** is an avenue that goes along the entire [coastline](/wiki/Coastline "Coastline") of Montevideo. The literal meaning of the Spanish word *rambla* is "avenue" or "watercourse", but in the Americas it is mostly used as "coastal avenue", and since all the southern [departments of Uruguay](/wiki/Departments_of_Uruguay "Departments of Uruguay") border either the Río de la Plata or the Atlantic Ocean, they all have *ramblas* as well. As an integral part of Montevidean identity, the Rambla has been included by Uruguay in the Indicative List of [World Heritage](/wiki/List_of_World_Heritage_Sites_in_the_Americas "List of World Heritage Sites in the Americas") sites,^[\[104\]](#cite_note-104)^ though it has not received this status. Previously, the entire Rambla was called *Rambla Naciones Unidas* ("United Nations"), but in recent times different names have been given to specific parts of it.{#cite_ref-104}

The Rambla is a very important site for recreation and leisure in Montevideo. Every day, a large number of people go there to take long strolls, jog, bicycle, roller skate, fish and even---in a special area---skateboard. Its 27-kilometer (17 mi) length makes it one of the longest esplanades in the world.^[\[105\]](#cite_note-Rambla-105)^{#cite_ref-Rambla_105-0}

Montevideo is noted for its beaches, which are particularly important because 60% of the population spends the summer in the city.^[\[105\]](#cite_note-Rambla-105)^ Its best-known beaches are Ramírez, [Pocitos](/wiki/Pocitos "Pocitos"), [Carrasco](/wiki/Carrasco,_Montevideo "Carrasco, Montevideo"), [Buceo](/wiki/Buceo "Buceo") and [Malvín](/wiki/Malv%C3%ADn "Malvín"). Further east and west are other beaches including the Colorada, Punta Espinillo, Punta Yeguas, Zabala and Santa Catarina.{#cite_ref-Rambla_105-1}  

#### Cemeteries {#Cemeteries}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit&section=24 "Edit section: Cemeteries")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/2016_cementerio_Montevideo.jpg/220px-2016_cementerio_Montevideo.jpg)](/wiki/File:2016_cementerio_Montevideo.jpg) Central Cemetery.

There are five large [cemeteries](/wiki/Cemetery "Cemetery") in Montevideo, all administered by the "Fúnebre y Necrópolis" annex of the Intendencia of Montevideo.^[\[106\]](#cite_note-106)^{#cite_ref-106}

The largest cemetery is the [Cementerio del Norte](/wiki/Cementerio_del_Norte,_Montevideo "Cementerio del Norte, Montevideo"), located in the northern-central part of the city. The [Central Cemetery](/wiki/Central_Cemetery_of_Montevideo "Central Cemetery of Montevideo") (Spanish: *Cementerio central* ), located in [Barrio Sur](/wiki/Barrio_Sur,_Montevideo "Barrio Sur, Montevideo") in the southern area of the city, is one of Uruguay's main cemeteries. It was one of the first cemeteries (in contrast to church graveyards) in the country, founded in 1835 at a time when burials were still carried out by the Catholic Church. It is the burial place of many of the most famous Uruguayans, such as [Eduardo Acevedo](/wiki/Eduardo_Blanco_Acevedo "Eduardo Blanco Acevedo"), [Delmira Agustini](/wiki/Delmira_Agustini "Delmira Agustini"), [Luis Batlle Berres](/wiki/Luis_Batlle_Berres "Luis Batlle Berres"), [José Batlle y Ordóñez](/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Batlle_y_Ord%C3%B3%C3%B1ez "José Batlle y Ordóñez"), [Juan Manuel Blanes](/wiki/Juan_Manuel_Blanes "Juan Manuel Blanes"), François Ducasse, father of [Comte de Lautréamont](/wiki/Comte_de_Lautr%C3%A9amont "Comte de Lautréamont") (Isidore Ducasse),^[\[107\]](#cite_note-107)^ [Luis Alberto de Herrera](/wiki/Luis_Alberto_de_Herrera "Luis Alberto de Herrera"), [Benito Nardone](/wiki/Benito_Nardone "Benito Nardone"), [José Enrique Rodó](/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Enrique_Rod%C3%B3 "José Enrique Rodó"), and [Juan Zorrilla de San Martín](/wiki/Juan_Zorrilla_de_San_Mart%C3%ADn "Juan Zorrilla de San Martín").{#cite_ref-107}

The other large cemeteries are the [Cementerio del Buceo](/wiki/Cementerio_del_Buceo "Cementerio del Buceo"), [Cementerio del Cerro](/wiki/Cementerio_del_Cerro,_Montevideo "Cementerio del Cerro, Montevideo"), and [Cementerio Paso Molino](/wiki/Cementerio_Paso_Molino "Cementerio Paso Molino"). [The British Cemetery Montevideo](/wiki/The_British_Cemetery_Montevideo "The British Cemetery Montevideo") (Cementerio Británico) is another of the oldest cemeteries in Uruguay, located in the [Buceo](/wiki/Buceo "Buceo") neighborhood. Many [noblemen](/wiki/Nobility "Nobility") and eminent persons are buried there. The cemetery originated when the Englishman Thomas Samuel Hood purchased a plot of land in the name of the English residents in 1828. However, in 1884 the government compensated the British by moving the cemetery to Buceo to accommodate city growth. A section of the cemetery, known as [British Cemetery Montevideo Soldiers and Sailors](/wiki/British_Cemetery_Montevideo_Soldiers_and_Sailors "British Cemetery Montevideo Soldiers and Sailors"), contains the graves of quite a number of sailors of different nationalities, although the majority are of British descent. One [United States Marine](/wiki/United_States_Marine_Corps "United States Marine Corps"), Henry de Costa, is buried here.^[\[108\]](#cite_note-108)^{#cite_ref-108}  

### Demographics {#Demographics}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit&section=25 "Edit section: Demographics")\]

In 1860, Montevideo had 57,913 inhabitants including a number of people of [African origin](/wiki/Afro-Uruguayan "Afro-Uruguayan") who had been brought as slaves and had gained their freedom around the middle of the century. By 1880, the population had quadrupled, mainly because of the great European immigration. In 1908, its population had grown massively to 309,331 inhabitants.^[\[109\]](#cite_note-Javier_Meneses_Silva-109)^ In the course of the 20th century the city continued to receive large numbers of European immigrants, especially Spanish and [Italian](/wiki/Italian_settlement_in_Uruguay "Italian settlement in Uruguay"), followed by Portuguese Brazilians, [French](/wiki/French_Uruguayan "French Uruguayan"), Germans, English, Irish, Swiss, Austrians, Poles, Dutch, [Greek](/wiki/Greeks_in_Uruguay "Greeks in Uruguay"), Hungarians, Russians, Croats, [Lebanese](/wiki/Lebanese_Uruguayan "Lebanese Uruguayan"), [Armenians](/wiki/Armenians_in_Uruguay "Armenians in Uruguay"), and Jews of various origins.^[\[110\]](#cite_note-rincondelvago-110)^ The last wave of immigrants occurred between 1945 and 1955.^[\[32\]](#cite_note-tacuycom-32)^{#cite_ref-tacuycom_32-3}

According to the census survey carried out between 15 June and 31 July 2004, Montevideo had a population of 1,325,968 persons, compared to Uruguay's total population of 3,241,003. The female population was 707,697 (53.4%) while the male population accounted for 618,271 (46.6%). The population had declined since the previous census carried out in 1996, with an average annual growth rate of −1.5 per thousand. The continual decline has been documented since the census period of 1975--1985, which showed a rate of −5.6 per thousand. The decrease is due in large part to lowered fertility, partly offset by mortality, and to a smaller degree in migration. The birth rate declined by 19% from 1996 (17 per thousand) to 2004 (13.8 per thousand). Similarly, the total fertility rate (TFR) declined from 2.24 in 1996 to 1.79 in 2004. However, mortality continued to fall with [life expectancy at birth](/wiki/Life_expectancy_at_birth "Life expectancy at birth") for both sexes increasing by 1.73 years.^[\[111\]](#cite_note-census2004pdf-111)^{#cite_ref-census2004pdf_111-0}

In the census of 2011, Montevideo had a population of 1,319,108.^[\[12\]](#cite_note-INEpop-12)^{#cite_ref-INEpop_12-1}
{#cite_ref-Javier_Meneses_Silva_109-1}

|  1860  |  1884   |                          1908                           |   1963    |   1975    |   1985    |   1996    |   2004    |   2011    |
|--------|---------|---------------------------------------------------------|-----------|-----------|-----------|-----------|-----------|-----------|
| 58,000 | 164,028 | 309,331^[\[109\]](#cite_note-Javier_Meneses_Silva-109)^ | 1,202,890 | 1,176,049 | 1,251,511 | 1,303,182 | 1,269,552 | 1,319,108 |

Source: *Instituto Nacional de Estadística de Uruguay* ^[\[43\]](#cite_note-stats-43)^{#cite_ref-stats_43-2}  

Government and politics {#Government_and_politics}
--------------------------------------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit&section=26 "Edit section: Government and politics")\]  

### Intendancy of Montevideo {#Intendancy_of_Montevideo}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit&section=27 "Edit section: Intendancy of Montevideo")\]  
Main article: [Intendancy of Montevideo](/wiki/Intendancy_of_Montevideo "Intendancy of Montevideo")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Intendencia_de_Montevideo_02.jpg/235px-Intendencia_de_Montevideo_02.jpg)](/wiki/File:Intendencia_de_Montevideo_02.jpg) The [Palacio Municipal](/wiki/Palacio_Municipal_(Montevideo) "Palacio Municipal (Montevideo)") is the [City Hall](/wiki/City_Hall "City Hall") of Montevideo.

The Intendancy of Montevideo was first created by a legal act of 18 December 1908.^[\[112\]](#cite_note-112)^ The municipality's first mayor (1909--1911) was Daniel Muñoz. Municipalities were abolished by the [Uruguayan Constitution of 1918](/wiki/Uruguayan_Constitution_of_1918 "Uruguayan Constitution of 1918"), effectively restored during the 1933 military coup of [Gabriel Terra](/wiki/Gabriel_Terra "Gabriel Terra"), and formally restored by the [1934 Constitution](/wiki/Uruguayan_Constitution_of_1934 "Uruguayan Constitution of 1934"). The [1952 Constitution](/wiki/Uruguayan_Constitution_of_1952 "Uruguayan Constitution of 1952") again decided to abolish the municipalities; it came into effect in February 1955. Municipalities were replaced by departmental councils, which consisted of a collegiate executive board with 7 members from Montevideo and 5 from the interior region. However, municipalities were revived under the 1967 Constitution and have operated continuously since that time.{#cite_ref-112}

Since 1990, Montevideo has been partially decentralized into 18 areas; administration and services for each area is provided by its Zonal Community Center (*Centro Comunal Zonal* , CCZ), which is subordinate to the Intendancy of Montevideo.^[\[113\]](#cite_note-113)^^[\[114\]](#cite_note-114)^ The boundaries of the municipal districts of Montevideo were created on 12 July 1993, and successively amended on 19 October 1993, 6 June 1994 and 10 November 1994. In 2010, the city CCZ were abolished and eight municipalities were created instead.{#cite_ref-114}

The city government of Montevideo performs several functions, including maintaining communications with the public, promoting culture, organizing society, caring for the environment and regulating traffic. The city hall is the [Palacio Municipal](/wiki/Palacio_Municipal_(Montevideo) "Palacio Municipal (Montevideo)") on 18 de Julio Avenue in the [Centro](/wiki/Centro,_Montevideo "Centro, Montevideo") area of Montevideo.^[\[115\]](#cite_note-115)^{#cite_ref-115}

The legislative branch of government, the Junta Departamental, or the Congress of Montevideo, governs the [Department of Montevideo](/wiki/Montevideo_Department "Montevideo Department"). The Junta, composed of 31 unsalaried elected members, is responsible for such things as the freedom of the citizens, the regulation of cultural activities, the naming of streets and public places, and the placement of monuments; it also responds to proposals of the Intendant in various circumstances.^[\[116\]](#cite_note-juntamvd.gub.uy-116)^ Its seat is the architecturally remarkable Casa de Francisco Gómez in Ciudad Vieja.^[\[116\]](#cite_note-juntamvd.gub.uy-116)^{#cite_ref-juntamvd.gub.uy_116-1}

A 2016 private ranking named *Subnational Legislative Online Opening Index* measured the data availability in official websites, scoring Montevideo as the second most open district nationally at 17.50 points.^[\[117\]](#cite_note-117)^{#cite_ref-117}  

### Intendants of Montevideo {#Intendants_of_Montevideo}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit&section=28 "Edit section: Intendants of Montevideo")\]  
Main article: [Intendant of Montevideo](/wiki/Intendant_of_Montevideo "Intendant of Montevideo")  
1. Daniel Muñoz (1909--1911)
2. Ramón V. Benzano (1911--1914)
3. Juan M. Aubriot (1914--1914)
4. Santiago Rivas (1914--1915)
5. Francisco Accinelli (1915--1919)
6. Alberto Dagnino (1933--1937)
7. Luis Alberto Zanzi (1937--1938)
8. Horacio Acosta y Lara (1938--1942)
9. Benigno Paiva (1942--1942)
10. Pedro Onetti (1942--1943)
11. Juan Pedro Fabini (1943--1947)
12. [Andrés Martínez Trueba](/wiki/Andr%C3%A9s_Mart%C3%ADnez_Trueba "Andrés Martínez Trueba") (1947--1948)
13. Álvaro Correa Moreno (1950--1951)
14. Germán Barbato (1951--1954)
15. Armando Malet (1954--1955)
16. Board members of the Concejo Departamental (1955--1967)
17. Glauco Segovia (1967--1967)
18. Carlos Bartolomé Herrera (1967--1969)
19. Oscar Víctor Rachetti (1969--1971)
20. E. Mario Peyrot (1971--1972)
21. Oscar Víctor Rachetti (1972--1983)
22. Juan Carlos Payssé (1983--1985)
23. Aquiles R. Lanza (1985--1985)
24. Julio Iglesias Álvarez (1985--1986)
25. Eduardo Fabini Jiménez (1989--1990)

27. Tabaré González (1994--1995)

29. Adolfo Pérez Piera (2005)

34. [Christian di Candia](/wiki/Christian_di_Candia "Christian di Candia") (2019--2020)
35. [Carolina Cosse](/wiki/Carolina_Cosse "Carolina Cosse") (2020-incumbent)  

Culture {#Culture}
------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit&section=29 "Edit section: Culture")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Teatro_Sol%C3%ADs%2C_interior_04.jpg/220px-Teatro_Sol%C3%ADs%2C_interior_04.jpg)](/wiki/File:Teatro_Sol%C3%ADs,_interior_04.jpg) [Solis Theatre](/wiki/Sol%C3%ADs_Theatre "Solís Theatre") in Montevideo

In recent years Montevideo nightlife has moved to Parque Rodó, where a large concentration of buildings cater for the recreational interests of young people during the night time. Under a presidential decree which went into effect on 1 March 2006, [smoking is prohibited](/wiki/Smoking_in_Uruguay "Smoking in Uruguay") in any public place with roofing,^[\[118\]](#cite_note-118)^ and there is a prohibition on the sale of alcohol in certain businesses from 21.00 to 9.00.^\[*[failed verification](/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability "Wikipedia:Verifiability")*\]^{#cite_ref-118}

Montevideo has been part of the [UNESCO Creative Cities Network](/wiki/Creative_Cities_Network "Creative Cities Network") in the area of Literature since December 2015.^[\[119\]](#cite_note-119)^^[\[120\]](#cite_note-120)^{#cite_ref-120}  

### The arts {#The_arts}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit&section=30 "Edit section: The arts")\]

Montevideo has a very rich architectural heritage and a number of writers, artists, and musicians. Uruguayan tango is a unique form of dance that originated in the neighborhoods of Montevideo towards the end of the 1800s. [Tango](/wiki/Tango_music "Tango music"), [candombe](/wiki/Candombe "Candombe") and [murga](/wiki/Murga "Murga") are the three main styles of music in this city. The city is also the center of the [cinema of Uruguay](/wiki/Cinema_of_Uruguay "Cinema of Uruguay"), which includes commercial, documentary and experimental films. There are two movie theater companies running seven cinemas,^[\[121\]](#cite_note-121)^^[\[122\]](#cite_note-122)^ around ten independent ones^[\[123\]](#cite_note-123)^ and four art film cinemas in the city.^[\[124\]](#cite_note-124)^ The theater of Uruguay is admired inside and outside Uruguayan borders. The [Solís Theatre](/wiki/Sol%C3%ADs_Theatre "Solís Theatre") is the most prominent theater in Uruguay and the oldest in South America.^[\[125\]](#cite_note-125)^ There are several notable theatrical companies and thousands of professional actors and amateurs. Montevideo playwrights produce dozens of works each year; of major note are [Mauricio Rosencof](/wiki/Mauricio_Rosencof "Mauricio Rosencof"), [Ana Magnabosco](/w/index.php?title=Ana_Magnabosco&action=edit&redlink=1 "Ana Magnabosco (page does not exist)") \[[es](https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ana_Magnabosco "es:Ana Magnabosco")\] and [Ricardo Prieto](/w/index.php?title=Ricardo_Prieto&action=edit&redlink=1 "Ricardo Prieto (page does not exist)") \[[es](https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ricardo_Prieto "es:Ricardo Prieto")\].{#cite_ref-125}  

#### Visual arts {#Visual_arts}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit&section=31 "Edit section: Visual arts")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Montevideo_painters.jpg/220px-Montevideo_painters.jpg)](/wiki/File:Montevideo_painters.jpg) Painter shop in Montevideo

The daily newspaper *El País* sponsors the Virtual Museum of Contemporary Uruguayan Art. The director and curator of the Museum presents exhibitions in "virtual spaces, supplemented by information, biographies, texts in English and Spanish".^[\[126\]](#cite_note-Arts-126)^{#cite_ref-Arts_126-0}

In the early 1970s (1973, to be particular) when the military junta took over power in Uruguay, art suffered in Montevideo. The art studios went into protest mode, with [Rimer Cardillo](/wiki/Rimer_Cardillo "Rimer Cardillo"), one of the country's leading artists, making the National Institute of Fine Arts, Montevideo a "hotbed of resistance". This resulted in the military junta coming down heavily on artists by closing the Fine Art Institute and carting away all the presses and other studio equipment. Consequently, the learning of fine arts was only in private studios run by people who had been let out of jail, in works of printing and on paper and also painting and sculpture. It resumed much later.^[\[127\]](#cite_note-Dorsky-127)^{#cite_ref-Dorsky_127-0}  

#### Literature {#Literature}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit&section=32 "Edit section: Literature")\]

The first public library in Montevideo was formed by the initial donation of the private library of Father José Manuel Pérez Castellano, who died in 1815. Its promoter, director and organizer was Father [Dámaso Antonio Larrañaga](/wiki/D%C3%A1maso_Antonio_Larra%C3%B1aga "Dámaso Antonio Larrañaga"), who also made a considerable donation along with donations from José Raimundo Guerra, as well as others from the Convent of San Francisco in [Salta](/wiki/Salta "Salta").^[\[128\]](#cite_note-128)^ In 1816 its stock was 5,000 volumes.^[\[129\]](#cite_note-129)^ The building of the [National Library of Uruguay](/wiki/National_Library_of_Uruguay "National Library of Uruguay") (*Biblioteca Pública de Uruguay* ) was designed by Luis Crespi in the [Neoclassical](/wiki/Neoclassical_architecture "Neoclassical architecture") style and occupies an area of 4,000 square meters (43,000 sq ft). Construction began in 1926 and it was inaugurated in 1964. Its collection amounts to 900,000 volumes.^[\[130\]](#cite_note-130)^^[\[131\]](#cite_note-131)^{#cite_ref-131}  

#### Authors {#Authors}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit&section=33 "Edit section: Authors")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Delmira_Agustini.jpg/170px-Delmira_Agustini.jpg)](/wiki/File:Delmira_Agustini.jpg) The poet [Delmira Agustini](/wiki/Delmira_Agustini "Delmira Agustini").

The city has a long and rich literary tradition. Although [Uruguayan literature](/wiki/Uruguayan_literature "Uruguayan literature") is not limited to the authors of the capital ([Horacio Quiroga](/wiki/Horacio_Quiroga "Horacio Quiroga") was born in [Salto](/wiki/Salto,_Uruguay "Salto, Uruguay") and [Mario Benedetti](/wiki/Mario_Benedetti "Mario Benedetti") in [Paso de los Toros](/wiki/Paso_de_los_Toros "Paso de los Toros"), for instance), Montevideo has been and is the center of the editorial and creative activity of literature.

In 1900, the city had a remarkable group of writers, including [José Enrique Rodó](/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Enrique_Rod%C3%B3 "José Enrique Rodó"), [Carlos Vaz Ferreira](/wiki/Carlos_Vaz_Ferreira "Carlos Vaz Ferreira"), [Julio Herrera y Reissig](/wiki/Julio_Herrera_y_Reissig "Julio Herrera y Reissig"), [Delmira Agustini](/wiki/Delmira_Agustini "Delmira Agustini") and [Felisberto Hernández](/wiki/Felisberto_Hern%C3%A1ndez "Felisberto Hernández"). Montevideo was then called the "Atenas del Plata" or the "[Athens](/wiki/Athens "Athens") of the Rio de la Plata".^[\[132\]](#cite_note-132)^{#cite_ref-132}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Eduardo_Galeano_-_conferenza_Vicenza_2.jpg/170px-Eduardo_Galeano_-_conferenza_Vicenza_2.jpg)](/wiki/File:Eduardo_Galeano_-_conferenza_Vicenza_2.jpg) The writer [Eduardo Galeano](/wiki/Eduardo_Galeano "Eduardo Galeano").

Among the outstanding authors of Montevideo of the second half of the 20th century are [Juan Carlos Onetti](/wiki/Juan_Carlos_Onetti "Juan Carlos Onetti"), [Antonio Larreta](/wiki/Antonio_Larreta "Antonio Larreta"), [Eduardo Galeano](/wiki/Eduardo_Galeano "Eduardo Galeano"), [Marosa di Giorgio](/wiki/Marosa_di_Giorgio "Marosa di Giorgio") and [Cristina Peri Rossi](/wiki/Cristina_Peri_Rossi "Cristina Peri Rossi").^[\[133\]](#cite_note-133)^{#cite_ref-133}

A new generation of writers has become known internationally in recent years. These include Eduardo Espina (essayist and poet), [Fernando Butazzoni](/wiki/Fernando_Butazzoni "Fernando Butazzoni") (novelist), [Rafael Courtoisie](/w/index.php?title=Rafael_Courtoisie&action=edit&redlink=1 "Rafael Courtoisie (page does not exist)") \[[es](https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rafael_Courtoisie "es:Rafael Courtoisie")\] (poet) and [Hugo Burel](/wiki/Hugo_Burel "Hugo Burel") (short story writer and novelist).  

#### Music {#Music}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit&section=34 "Edit section: Music")\]

In Montevideo, as throughout the Rio de Plata region, the most popular forms of music are [tango](/wiki/Tango_music "Tango music"), [milonga](/wiki/Milonga_(music) "Milonga (music)") and *[vals criollo](/wiki/Vals_criollo "Vals criollo")* . Many notable songs originated in Montevideo including "El Tango supremo", "La Cumparsita", "La Milonga", "La Puñalada" and "[Desde el Alma](/wiki/Desde_el_Alma "Desde el Alma")", composed by notable Montevideo musicians such as [Gerardo Matos Rodríguez](/wiki/Gerardo_Matos_Rodr%C3%ADguez "Gerardo Matos Rodríguez"), [Pintín Castellanos](/wiki/Pint%C3%ADn_Castellanos "Pintín Castellanos") and [Rosita Melo](/wiki/Rosita_Melo "Rosita Melo").^[\[134\]](#cite_note-SC1-134)^ Tango is deeply ingrained in the cultural life of the city and is the theme for many of the bars and restaurants in the city. 20th. century composers like three-time [Grammy](/wiki/Grammy_Awards "Grammy Awards") nominated [Miguel del Aguila](/wiki/Miguel_del_%C3%81guila "Miguel del Águila") have taken Uruguayan tango to international classical music audiences. *Fun Fun' Bar* , established in 1935, is one of the most important places for tango in Uruguay as is *El Farolito* , located in the old part of the city and *Joventango* , *Café Las Musas* , *Garufa* and *Vieja Viola* .^[\[134\]](#cite_note-SC1-134)^ The city is also home to the Montevideo Jazz Festival and has the Bancaria Jazz Club bar catering for jazz enthusiasts.{#cite_ref-SC1_134-1}  

### Cuisine {#Cuisine}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit&section=35 "Edit section: Cuisine")\]  
Main article: [Cuisine of Montevideo](/wiki/Cuisine_of_Montevideo "Cuisine of Montevideo")

The center of traditional Uruguayan food and beverage in Montevideo is the Mercado del Puerto ("Port Market"). Beef is very important in Uruguayan cuisine and an essential part of many dishes. A *[torta frita](/wiki/Torta_frita "Torta frita")* is a pan-fried cake consumed in Montevideo and throughout Uruguay. It is generally circular, with a small cut in the center for cooking, and is made from wheat flour, yeast, water and sugar or salt.^[\[135\]](#cite_note-135)^ Montevideo has a variety of restaurants, from traditional [Uruguayan cuisine](/wiki/Uruguayan_cuisine "Uruguayan cuisine") to [Japanese cuisine](/wiki/Japanese_cuisine "Japanese cuisine").{#cite_ref-135}
