### Recreation {#Recreation}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit&section=37 "Edit section: Recreation")\]  

#### Museums {#Museums}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit&section=38 "Edit section: Museums")\]  
Main article: [List of museums in Montevideo](/wiki/List_of_museums_in_Montevideo "List of museums in Montevideo")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Cabildo_de_Montevideo.jpg/220px-Cabildo_de_Montevideo.jpg)](/wiki/File:Cabildo_de_Montevideo.jpg) Fountain in the entry of the Cabildo

The Centro Cultural de España, as well as [Asturian](/wiki/Asturias "Asturias") and cultural centers, testify to Montevideo's considerable Spanish heritage. Montevideo also has important museums including [Museo Torres García](/wiki/Museo_Torres_Garc%C3%ADa "Museo Torres García"),^[\[136\]](#cite_note-136)^ [Museo José Gurvich](/w/index.php?title=Museo_Jos%C3%A9_Gurvich&action=edit&redlink=1 "Museo José Gurvich (page does not exist)") \[[es](https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Museo_Gurvich "es:Museo Gurvich")\], [Museo Nacional de Artes Visuales](/wiki/Museo_Nacional_de_Artes_Visuales "Museo Nacional de Artes Visuales") and [Museo Juan Manuel Blanes](/wiki/Juan_Manuel_Blanes_Museum "Juan Manuel Blanes Museum") etc.{#cite_ref-136}

The [Montevideo Cabildo](/wiki/Montevideo_Cabildo "Montevideo Cabildo") was the [seat of government](/wiki/Seat_of_government "Seat of government") during the colonial times of the [Viceroyalty of the Río de la Plata](/wiki/Viceroyalty_of_the_R%C3%ADo_de_la_Plata "Viceroyalty of the Río de la Plata"). It is located in front of [Constitution Square](/wiki/Constitution_Square_(Montevideo) "Constitution Square (Montevideo)"), in Ciudad Vieja.^[\[74\]](#cite_note-travel-74)^ Built between 1804 and 1869 in Neoclassical style, with a series of [Doric](/wiki/Doric_columns "Doric columns") and [Ionic](/wiki/Ionic_columns "Ionic columns") columns, it became a National Heritage Site in 1975. In 1958, the Municipal Historic Museum and Archive was inaugurated here. It features three permanent [city museum](/wiki/City_museum "City museum") exhibitions, as well as temporary art exhibitions, cultural events, seminars, symposiums and forums.^[\[137\]](#cite_note-137)^{#cite_ref-137}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Palacio_Taranco_meeting.jpg/170px-Palacio_Taranco_meeting.jpg)](/wiki/File:Palacio_Taranco_meeting.jpg) Uruguayan officials conversing at a meeting at the Palacio Taranco, 6 November 2010

The [Palacio Taranco](/wiki/Palacio_Taranco "Palacio Taranco") is located in front of the [Plaza Zabala](/wiki/Plaza_Zabala "Plaza Zabala"), in the heart of Ciudad Vieja. It was erected in the early 20th century as the residence of the Ortiz Taranco brothers on the ruins of Montevideo's first theater (of 1793), during a period in which the architectural style was influenced by French architecture. The palace was designed by French architects [Charles Louis Girault](/wiki/Charles_Louis_Girault "Charles Louis Girault") and [Jules-Léon Chifflot](/w/index.php?title=Jules-L%C3%A9on_Chifflot&action=edit&redlink=1 "Jules-Léon Chifflot (page does not exist)") \[[fr](https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jules-L%C3%A9on_Chifflot "fr:Jules-Léon Chifflot")\] who also designed the [Petit Palais](/wiki/Petit_Palais "Petit Palais") and the [Arc de Triomphe](/wiki/Arc_de_Triomphe "Arc de Triomphe") in Paris. It passed to the city from the heirs of the Tarancos in 1943, along with its precious collection of Uruguayan furniture and draperies and was deemed by the city as an ideal place for a museum; in 1972 it became the Museum of Decorative Arts of Montevideo and in 1975 it became a National Heritage Site.^[\[138\]](#cite_note-Frommers-138)^^[\[139\]](#cite_note-139)^ The Decorative Arts Museum has an important collection of European paintings and decorative arts, ancient [Greek](/wiki/Ancient_Greece "Ancient Greece") and [Roman art](/wiki/Roman_art "Roman art") and Islamic [ceramics](/wiki/Ceramic_art "Ceramic art") of the 10th--18th century from the area of present-day Iran.^[\[126\]](#cite_note-Arts-126)^ The palace is often used as a meeting place by the Uruguayan government.{#cite_ref-Arts_126-1}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/MuseoHistoricoNacionalMontevideo.jpg/220px-MuseoHistoricoNacionalMontevideo.jpg)](/wiki/File:MuseoHistoricoNacionalMontevideo.jpg) Museo Historico Nacional de Montevideo

The National History Museum of Montevideo is located in the historical residence of General [Fructuoso Rivera](/wiki/Fructuoso_Rivera "Fructuoso Rivera"). It exhibits artifacts related to the history of Uruguay.^[\[74\]](#cite_note-travel-74)^ In a process begun in 1998, the National Museum of Natural History (1837) and the National Museum of Anthropology (1981), merged in 2001, becoming the National Museum of Natural History and Anthropology. In July 2009, the two institutions again became independent.^[\[140\]](#cite_note-MuseosNacionales-140)^ The Historical Museum has annexed eight historical houses in the city, five of which are located in the Ciudad Vieja. One of them, on the same block with the main building, is the historic residence of Antonio Montero, which houses the Museo Romantico.^[\[141\]](#cite_note-141)^ Also nearby is the Museo Casa de José Garibaldi where [Giuseppe Garibaldi](/wiki/Giuseppe_Garibaldi "Giuseppe Garibaldi") lived in the 1840s while participating in the [Uruguayan Civil War](/wiki/Uruguayan_Civil_War "Uruguayan Civil War").^[\[142\]](#cite_note-142)^{#cite_ref-142}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Museo_Torres_Garcia.jpg/213px-Museo_Torres_Garcia.jpg)](/wiki/File:Museo_Torres_Garcia.jpg) Museo Torres García

The [Museo Torres García](/wiki/Museo_Torres_Garc%C3%ADa "Museo Torres García") is located in the Old Town, and exhibits [Joaquín Torres García](/wiki/Joaqu%C3%ADn_Torres_Garc%C3%ADa "Joaquín Torres García")'s unusual portraits of historical icons and [cubist](/wiki/Cubism "Cubism") paintings akin to those of [Picasso](/wiki/Pablo_Picasso "Pablo Picasso") and [Braque](/wiki/Georges_Braque "Georges Braque").^[\[143\]](#cite_note-about-143)^ The museum was established by Manolita Piña Torres, the widow of Torres Garcia, after his death in 1949. She also set up the García Torres Foundation, a private non-profit organization that organizes the paintings, drawings, original writings, archives, objects and furniture designed by the painter as well as the photographs, magazines and publications related to him.^[\[144\]](#cite_note-Torres_Garcia-144)^{#cite_ref-Torres_Garcia_144-0}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Museo_Naval_Montevideo.JPG/220px-Museo_Naval_Montevideo.JPG)](/wiki/File:Museo_Naval_Montevideo.JPG) [Museo Naval de Montevideo](/wiki/Museo_Naval_de_Montevideo "Museo Naval de Montevideo")

There are several other important art museums in Montevideo. The [Centro de Fotografía de Montevideo](/wiki/Centro_de_Fotograf%C3%ADa_de_Montevideo "Centro de Fotografía de Montevideo") (CdF) is a museum, archive, and gallery for historic and contemporary photography with twelve outdoor exhibition spaces in various Montevideo neighborhoods as well as four galleries in its downtown headquarters. The [National Museum of Visual Arts](/wiki/National_Museum_of_Visual_Arts_(Uruguay) "National Museum of Visual Arts (Uruguay)") in Parque Rodó has Uruguay's largest collection of paintings.^[\[77\]](#cite_note-Sights-77)^^[\[126\]](#cite_note-Arts-126)^ The [Juan Manuel Blanes Museum](/wiki/Juan_Manuel_Blanes_Museum "Juan Manuel Blanes Museum") was founded in 1930, the 100th anniversary of the first [Constitution of Uruguay](/wiki/Constitution_of_Uruguay "Constitution of Uruguay"), significant with regard to the fact that [Juan Manuel Blanes](/wiki/Juan_Manuel_Blanes "Juan Manuel Blanes") painted Uruguayan patriotic themes. In the back of the museum is a Japanese Garden with a pond where there are over a hundred [carp](/wiki/Carp "Carp").^[\[145\]](#cite_note-145)^ The Museo de Historia del Arte, located in the Palacio Municipal, features replicas of ancient monuments and exhibits a varied collection of artifacts from Egypt, Mesopotamia, Persia, Greece, Rome and Native American cultures including local finds of the pre-Columbian period.^[\[146\]](#cite_note-146)^ The Museo Municipal Precolombino y Colonial, in the Ciudad Vieja, has preserved collections of the archeological finds from excavations carried out by Uruguayan archeologist Antonio Taddei. These antiquaries are exhibits of pre-Columbian art of Latin America, painting and sculpture from the 17th and 18th century mostly from Mexico, [Peru](/wiki/Peru "Peru") and Brazil.^[\[126\]](#cite_note-Arts-126)^ The Museo de Arte Contempo has small exhibits of modern Uruguayan painting and sculpture.^[\[77\]](#cite_note-Sights-77)^{#cite_ref-Sights_77-2}

There are also other types of museums in the city. The Museo del Gaucho y de la Moneda, located in the Centro, has distinctive displays of the historical culture of Uruguay's [gauchos](/wiki/Gaucho "Gaucho"), their horse gear, silver work and *[mate](/wiki/Yerba_mate "Yerba mate")* (tea), gourds, and *bombillas* (drinking straws) in odd designs.^[\[77\]](#cite_note-Sights-77)^ The Museo Naval, is located on the eastern waterfront in Buceo and offers exhibits depicting the maritime history of Uruguay.^[\[77\]](#cite_note-Sights-77)^ The Museo del Automóvil, belonging to the Automobile Club of Uruguay, has a rich collection of vintage cars which includes a 1910 [Hupmobile](/wiki/Hupmobile "Hupmobile").^[\[147\]](#cite_note-147)^ The Museo y Parque Fernando García in Carrasco, a transport and automobile museum, includes old horse carriages and some early automobiles.^[\[148\]](#cite_note-148)^ The Castillo Pittamiglio, with an unusual façade, highlights the eccentric legacy of Humberto Pittamiglio, local alchemist and architect.^[\[77\]](#cite_note-Sights-77)^{#cite_ref-Sights_77-5}  

#### Festivals {#Festivals}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit&section=39 "Edit section: Festivals")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Las_Llamadas_-_Carnaval_2011_-_110203-0690-jikatu.jpg/228px-Las_Llamadas_-_Carnaval_2011_-_110203-0690-jikatu.jpg)](/wiki/File:Las_Llamadas_-_Carnaval_2011_-_110203-0690-jikatu.jpg) Carnival drummers. [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/La_Gozadera_Montevideo_Llamadas_Carnaval_2012_17.jpg/232px-La_Gozadera_Montevideo_Llamadas_Carnaval_2012_17.jpg)](/wiki/File:La_Gozadera_Montevideo_Llamadas_Carnaval_2012_17.jpg) Carnival dancer and drummers.  
See also: [Uruguayan Carnival](/wiki/Uruguayan_Carnival "Uruguayan Carnival")

As the capital of Uruguay, Montevideo is home to a number of festivals and carnivals including a Gaucho festival when people ride through the streets on horseback in traditional gaucho gear. The major annual festival is the annual [Montevideo Carnival](/wiki/Uruguayan_Carnival "Uruguayan Carnival") which is part of the national festival of Carnival Week, celebrated throughout Uruguay, with central activities in the capital, Montevideo. Officially, the public holiday lasts for two days on Carnival Monday and [Shrove Tuesday](/wiki/Shrove_Tuesday "Shrove Tuesday") preceding [Ash Wednesday](/wiki/Ash_Wednesday "Ash Wednesday"), but due to the prominence of the festival, most shops and businesses close for the entire week.^[\[149\]](#cite_note-Carnaval-149)^ During carnival there are many open-air stage performances and competitions and the streets and houses are vibrantly decorated. "Tablados" or popular scenes, both fixed and movable, are erected in the whole city.^[\[149\]](#cite_note-Carnaval-149)^ Notable displays include "Desfile de las Llamadas" ("Parade of the Calls"), which is a grand united parade held on the south part of downtown, where it used to be a common ritual back in the early 20th century.^[\[149\]](#cite_note-Carnaval-149)^ Due to the scale of the festival, preparation begins as early as December with an election of the "zonal beauty queens" to appear in the carnival.^[\[149\]](#cite_note-Carnaval-149)^{#cite_ref-Carnaval_149-3}  

#### Sports {#Sports}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit&section=40 "Edit section: Sports")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Estadio_Centenario_%28vista_a%C3%A9rea%29.jpg/262px-Estadio_Centenario_%28vista_a%C3%A9rea%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Estadio_Centenario_(vista_a%C3%A9rea).jpg) [Estadio Centenario](/wiki/Estadio_Centenario "Estadio Centenario")

[Estadio Centenario](/wiki/Estadio_Centenario "Estadio Centenario"), the national [football](/wiki/Association_football "Association football") stadium in [Parque Batlle](/wiki/Parque_Batlle "Parque Batlle"), was opened in 1930 for the first [World Cup](/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup "FIFA World Cup"), as well as to commemorate the centennial of [Uruguay's first constitution](/wiki/Uruguay#Struggle_for_independence "Uruguay"). In this World Cup, Uruguay won the title game against Argentina by 4 goals to 2.^[\[150\]](#cite_note-Burford-150)^ The stadium has 70,000 seats.^[\[91\]](#cite_note-Box-91)^ It is listed by [FIFA](/wiki/FIFA "FIFA") as one of the football world's classic stadiums, along with [Maracanã](/wiki/Est%C3%A1dio_do_Maracan%C3%A3 "Estádio do Maracanã"), [Wembley Stadium](/wiki/Wembley_Stadium "Wembley Stadium"), [San Siro](/wiki/San_Siro "San Siro"), [Estadio Azteca](/wiki/Estadio_Azteca "Estadio Azteca"), and [Santiago Bernabéu Stadium](/wiki/Santiago_Bernab%C3%A9u_Stadium "Santiago Bernabéu Stadium").^[\[151\]](#cite_note-151)^ A museum located within the football stadium has exhibits of memorabilia from Uruguay's 1930 and 1950 World Cup championships. Museum tickets give access to the stadium, stands, locker rooms and playing field.^[\[77\]](#cite_note-Sights-77)^{#cite_ref-Sights_77-6}

Between 1935 and 1938, the athletics track and the municipal [velodrome](/wiki/Velodrome "Velodrome") were completed within Parque Batlle. The Tabaré Athletic Club is occasionally made over as a carnival theater using impermanent materials.^[\[152\]](#cite_note-Remedi-152)^^[\[153\]](#cite_note-153)^{#cite_ref-153}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/PSG_rugby_seven_punta.JPG/220px-PSG_rugby_seven_punta.JPG)](/wiki/File:PSG_rugby_seven_punta.JPG) Rugby in Montevideo

Today the vast majority of teams in the [Primera División](/wiki/Uruguayan_Primera_Divisi%C3%B3n "Uruguayan Primera División") and [Segunda División](/wiki/Uruguayan_Segunda_Divisi%C3%B3n "Uruguayan Segunda División") come from Montevideo, including [Nacional](/wiki/Club_Nacional_de_Football "Club Nacional de Football"), [Peñarol](/wiki/Club_Atl%C3%A9tico_Pe%C3%B1arol "Club Atlético Peñarol"), [Central Español](/wiki/Central_Espa%C3%B1ol "Central Español"), [Cerrito](/wiki/Club_Sportivo_Cerrito "Club Sportivo Cerrito"), [Cerro](/wiki/Club_Atl%C3%A9tico_Cerro "Club Atlético Cerro"), [Danubio](/wiki/Danubio_F%C3%BAtbol_Club "Danubio Fútbol Club"), [Defensor Sporting](/wiki/Defensor_Sporting_Club "Defensor Sporting Club"), [Atlético Fénix](/wiki/Centro_Atl%C3%A9tico_F%C3%A9nix "Centro Atlético Fénix"), [Liverpool](/wiki/Liverpool_F%C3%BAtbol_Club "Liverpool Fútbol Club"), [Wanderers](/wiki/Montevideo_Wanderers_F.C. "Montevideo Wanderers F.C."), [Racing](/wiki/Racing_Club_de_Montevideo "Racing Club de Montevideo"), [River Plate](/wiki/Club_Atl%C3%A9tico_River_Plate_(Uruguay) "Club Atlético River Plate (Uruguay)"), [Club Atlético Torque](/wiki/Club_Atl%C3%A9tico_Torque "Club Atlético Torque"), [Boston River](/wiki/Boston_River "Boston River") and [Rampla Juniors](/wiki/Rampla_Juniors_F%C3%BAtbol_Club "Rampla Juniors Fútbol Club").

Besides Estadio Centenario, other stadiums include [Gran Parque Central](/wiki/Estadio_Gran_Parque_Central "Estadio Gran Parque Central"), [Estadio Campeón del Siglo](/wiki/Estadio_Campe%C3%B3n_del_Siglo "Estadio Campeón del Siglo"), [Belvedere](/wiki/Estadio_Belvedere "Estadio Belvedere"), [Complejo Rentistas](/wiki/Estadio_Complejo_Rentistas "Estadio Complejo Rentistas"), [Jardines del Hipódromo](/wiki/Estadio_Jardines_del_Hip%C3%B3dromo "Estadio Jardines del Hipódromo"), [José Pedro Damiani](/wiki/Estadio_Jos%C3%A9_Pedro_Damiani "Estadio José Pedro Damiani"), ["La Bombonera"](/wiki/Estadio_La_Bombonera_(Montevideo) "Estadio La Bombonera (Montevideo)"), [Luis Franzini](/wiki/Estadio_Luis_Franzini "Estadio Luis Franzini"), [Luis Tróccoli](/wiki/Estadio_Luis_Tr%C3%B3ccoli "Estadio Luis Tróccoli") and the park stadiums of [Abraham Paladino](/wiki/Estadio_Parque_Abraham_Paladino "Estadio Parque Abraham Paladino"), [Alfredo Víctor Viera](/wiki/Estadio_Parque_Alfredo_V%C3%ADctor_Viera "Estadio Parque Alfredo Víctor Viera"), [Omar Saroldi](/wiki/Estadio_Parque_Federico_Omar_Saroldi "Estadio Parque Federico Omar Saroldi"), [José Nasazzi](/wiki/Estadio_Parque_Jos%C3%A9_Nasazzi "Estadio Parque José Nasazzi"), [Osvaldo Roberto](/wiki/Estadio_Parque_Osvaldo_Roberto "Estadio Parque Osvaldo Roberto"), [Maracaná](/wiki/Estadio_Parque_Maracan%C3%A1 "Estadio Parque Maracaná") and [Palermo](/wiki/Estadio_Parque_Palermo "Estadio Parque Palermo").

The city has a tradition as host of major international basketball tournaments including the official [1967 FIBA World Cup](/wiki/1967_FIBA_World_Cup "1967 FIBA World Cup") and the [1988](/wiki/1988_Tournament_of_the_Americas "1988 Tournament of the Americas") [1997](/wiki/1997_Tournament_of_the_Americas "1997 Tournament of the Americas") and 2017 editions of the official [Americas Basketball Championship](/wiki/Americas_Basketball_Championship "Americas Basketball Championship").

The [Uruguayan Basketball League](/wiki/Uruguayan_Basketball_League "Uruguayan Basketball League") is headquartered in Montevideo and most of its teams are from the city, including [Defensor Sporting](/wiki/Defensor_Sporting_Club "Defensor Sporting Club"), [Biguá](/wiki/Club_Bigu%C3%A1 "Club Biguá"), [Atlético Aguada](/wiki/Club_Atl%C3%A9tico_Aguada "Club Atlético Aguada"), [Goes](/wiki/Club_Atl%C3%A9tico_Goes "Club Atlético Goes"), [Malvín](/wiki/Club_Malv%C3%ADn "Club Malvín"), [Unión Atlética](/w/index.php?title=Uni%C3%B3n_Atl%C3%A9tica&action=edit&redlink=1 "Unión Atlética (page does not exist)") \[[es](https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Club_Uni%C3%B3n_Atl%C3%A9tica "es:Club Unión Atlética")\], and [Trouville](/wiki/Club_Trouville "Club Trouville"). Montevideo is also a center of [rugby](/wiki/Rugby_football "Rugby football"); [equestrianism](/wiki/Equestrianism "Equestrianism"), which regained importance in Montevideo after the [Maroñas Racecourse](/wiki/Maro%C3%B1as_Racecourse "Maroñas Racecourse") reopened; golf, with the Club de Punta Carretas; and yachting, with the [Puerto del Buceo](/wiki/Puerto_del_Buceo "Puerto del Buceo"), an ideal place to moor yachts. The Golf Club of Punta Carretas was founded in 1894 covers all the area encircled by the west side of Bulevar Artigas, the Rambla (Montevideo's promenade) and the Parque Rodó (Fun Fair).^[\[103\]](#cite_note-HCV-103)^{#cite_ref-HCV_103-1}  

### Religion {#Religion}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit&section=41 "Edit section: Religion")\]

The religion with most followers in Montevideo is Roman Catholicism and has been so since the foundation of the city. The [Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Montevideo](/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Montevideo "Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Montevideo") was created as the [Apostolic Vicariate](/wiki/Apostolic_vicariate "Apostolic vicariate") of Montevideo in 1830. The vicariate was promoted to the Diocese of Montevideo on 13 July 1878.^[\[154\]](#cite_note-154)^ [Pope Leo XIII](/wiki/Pope_Leo_XIII "Pope Leo XIII") elevated it to the rank of a [metropolitan archdiocese](/wiki/Metropolitan_bishop "Metropolitan bishop") on 14 April 1897. The new archdiocese became the [Metropolitan](/wiki/Metropolitan_bishop "Metropolitan bishop") of the [suffragan sees](/wiki/Suffragan_bishop "Suffragan bishop") of [Canelones](/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Canelones "Roman Catholic Diocese of Canelones"), [Florida](/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Florida "Roman Catholic Diocese of Florida"), [Maldonado--Punta del Este](/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Maldonado%E2%80%93Punta_del_Este "Roman Catholic Diocese of Maldonado–Punta del Este"), [Melo](/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Melo "Roman Catholic Diocese of Melo"), [Mercedes](/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Mercedes "Roman Catholic Diocese of Mercedes"), [Minas](/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Minas "Roman Catholic Diocese of Minas"), [Salto](/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Salto "Roman Catholic Diocese of Salto"), [San José de Mayo](/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_San_Jos%C3%A9_de_Mayo "Roman Catholic Diocese of San José de Mayo"), [Tacuarembó](/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Tacuaremb%C3%B3 "Roman Catholic Diocese of Tacuarembó").{#cite_ref-154}

Montevideo is the only archdiocese in Uruguay and, as its [Ordinary](/wiki/Ordinary_(officer) "Ordinary (officer)"), the archbishop is also [Primate](/wiki/Primate_(bishop) "Primate (bishop)") of the [Catholic Church in Uruguay](/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_Uruguay "Roman Catholicism in Uruguay"). The archdiocese's [mother church](/wiki/Mother_Church "Mother Church") and thus seat of its archbishop is [Catedral de la Inmaculada Concepción y San Felipe y Santiago](/wiki/Catedral_de_la_Inmaculada_Concepci%C3%B3n_y_San_Felipe_y_Santiago "Catedral de la Inmaculada Concepción y San Felipe y Santiago"). Church and state are officially separated since 1916 in Uruguay. As of 2010^[\[update\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit)^, the Archbishop of Montevideo is [Daniel Fernando Sturla Berhouet](/wiki/Daniel_Fernando_Sturla_Berhouet "Daniel Fernando Sturla Berhouet"), [SDB](/wiki/Salesians_of_Don_Bosco "Salesians of Don Bosco"), since his appointment on 11 February 2014.^[\[155\]](#cite_note-155)^{#cite_ref-155}

Other religious faiths in Montevideo are [Protestantism](/wiki/Protestantism "Protestantism"), [Umbanda](/wiki/Umbanda "Umbanda"), [Judaism](/wiki/Judaism "Judaism"), and there are many people who define themselves as [Atheists](/wiki/Atheism "Atheism") and [Agnostics](/wiki/Agnosticism "Agnosticism"), while others profess "believing in God but without religion".^[\[156\]](#cite_note-enha_rel-156)^{#cite_ref-enha_rel_156-0}  

#### Montevideo Metropolitan Cathedral {#Montevideo_Metropolitan_Cathedral}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit&section=42 "Edit section: Montevideo Metropolitan Cathedral")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Catedralmontevideo.jpg/175px-Catedralmontevideo.jpg)](/wiki/File:Catedralmontevideo.jpg) Cathedral Interior  
Main article: [Montevideo Metropolitan Cathedral](/wiki/Montevideo_Metropolitan_Cathedral "Montevideo Metropolitan Cathedral")

The Montevideo Metropolitan Cathedral is the main Roman Catholic church of Montevideo. It is located in Ciudad Vieja, immediately across [Constitution Square](/wiki/Constitution_Square_(Montevideo) "Constitution Square (Montevideo)") from the [Cabildo](/wiki/Montevideo_Cabildo "Montevideo Cabildo"). In 1740 a brick church was built on the site. In 1790, the foundation was laid for the current neoclassical structure. The church was consecrated in 1804.^[\[74\]](#cite_note-travel-74)^ Bicentennial celebrations were held in 2004.{#cite_ref-travel_74-4}

In 1897, [Pope Leo XIII](/wiki/Pope_Leo_XIII "Pope Leo XIII") elevated the church to Metropolitan Cathedral status. Important ceremonies are conducted under the direction of the Archbishop of Montevideo. Weddings and choral concerts are held here and the parish priest conducts the routine functions of the cathedral. In the 19th century, its precincts were also used as a burial place of famous people who died in the city. For decades, the prison and the nearby [Punta Carretas parish church](/wiki/Punta_Carretas "Punta Carretas") were the only major buildings in the neighborhood.  

#### Nuestra Señora del Sagrado Corazón {#Nuestra_Se.C3.B1ora_del_Sagrado_Coraz.C3.B3n}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit&section=43 "Edit section: Nuestra Señora del Sagrado Corazón")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/2016_fachada_de_la_Iglesia_de_Nuestra_Se%C3%B1ora_del_Sagrado_Coraz%C3%B3n_de_Montevido.jpg/209px-2016_fachada_de_la_Iglesia_de_Nuestra_Se%C3%B1ora_del_Sagrado_Coraz%C3%B3n_de_Montevido.jpg)](/wiki/File:2016_fachada_de_la_Iglesia_de_Nuestra_Se%C3%B1ora_del_Sagrado_Coraz%C3%B3n_de_Montevido.jpg) Punta Carretas Church

Nuestra Señora del Sagrado Corazón ("Our Lady of the Sacred Heart"), also known as Iglesia Punta Carretas ("Punta Carretas Church"), was built between 1917 and 1927 in the Romanesque Revival style. The church was originally part of the [Order of Friars Minor Capuchin](/wiki/Order_of_Friars_Minor_Capuchin "Order of Friars Minor Capuchin"), but is presently in the parish of the Ecclesiastic Curia. Its location is at the corner of Solano García and José Ellauri. It has a nave and aisles. The roof has many vaults. During the construction of the Punta Carretas Shopping complex, major cracks developed in the structure of the church as a result of differential foundation settlement.^[\[103\]](#cite_note-HCV-103)^^[\[157\]](#cite_note-157)^{#cite_ref-157}  

Economy {#Economy}
------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit&section=44 "Edit section: Economy")\]

*[Main Article: Economy of Uruguay](/wiki/Economy_of_Uruguay "Economy of Uruguay")*

As the capital of Uruguay, Montevideo is the economic and political center of the country. Most of the largest and wealthiest businesses in Uruguay have their headquarters in the city. Since the 1990s the city has undergone rapid economic development and modernization, including two of Uruguay's most important buildings---the [World Trade Center Montevideo](/wiki/World_Trade_Center_Montevideo "World Trade Center Montevideo") (1998),^[\[158\]](#cite_note-158)^ and [Telecommunications Tower](/wiki/Telecommunications_Tower_(Montevideo) "Telecommunications Tower (Montevideo)") (2000), the headquarters of Uruguay's government-owned telecommunications company [ANTEL](/wiki/ANTEL "ANTEL"), increasing the city's integration into the global marketplace.^[\[159\]](#cite_note-159)^{#cite_ref-159}

The [Port of Montevideo](/wiki/Port_of_Montevideo "Port of Montevideo"), in the northern part of Ciudad Vieja, is one of the major ports of South America and plays a very important role in the city's economy.^[\[160\]](#cite_note-160)^^[\[161\]](#cite_note-161)^ The port has been growing rapidly and consistently at an average annual rate of 14 percent due to an increase in foreign trade. The city has received a US$20 million loan from the [Inter-American Development Bank](/wiki/Inter-American_Development_Bank "Inter-American Development Bank") to modernize the port, increase its size and efficiency, and enable lower maritime and river transportation costs.^[\[162\]](#cite_note-iadb-162)^{#cite_ref-iadb_162-0}

The most important state-owned companies headquartered in Montevideo are: [AFE](/wiki/State_Railways_Administration_of_Uruguay "State Railways Administration of Uruguay") (railways),^[\[163\]](#cite_note-163)^ [ANCAP](/wiki/ANCAP_(Uruguay) "ANCAP (Uruguay)") (Energy),^[\[164\]](#cite_note-164)^ Administracion Nacional de Puertos (Ports), [ANTEL](/wiki/ANTEL "ANTEL") (telecommunications),^[\[165\]](#cite_note-165)^ [BHU](/wiki/Banco_Hipotecario_del_Uruguay "Banco Hipotecario del Uruguay") (savings and loan),^[\[166\]](#cite_note-166)^ [BROU](/wiki/Banco_de_la_Rep%C3%BAblica_Oriental_del_Uruguay "Banco de la República Oriental del Uruguay") (bank),^[\[167\]](#cite_note-167)^ BSE (insurance),^[\[168\]](#cite_note-168)^ OSE (water \& sewage),^[\[169\]](#cite_note-169)^ [UTE](/wiki/UTE "UTE") (electricity).^[\[170\]](#cite_note-170)^ These companies operate under public law, using a legal entity defined in the Uruguayan Constitution called *Ente Autonomo* ("autonomous entity"). The government also owns part of other companies operating under private law, such as those owned wholly or partially by the CND (National Development Corporation).{#cite_ref-170}

Banking has traditionally been one of the strongest service export sectors in Uruguay: the country was once dubbed "the Switzerland of America",^[\[171\]](#cite_note-171)^ mainly for its banking sector and stability, although that stability has been threatened in the 21st century by the recent global economic climate.^[\[172\]](#cite_note-172)^ The largest bank in Uruguay is Banco Republica (BROU), based in Montevideo.^[\[173\]](#cite_note-173)^ 9 private banks, most of them branches of international banks, operate in the country ([Banco Santander](/wiki/Banco_Santander "Banco Santander"), [BBVA](/wiki/Banco_Bilbao_Vizcaya_Argentaria "Banco Bilbao Vizcaya Argentaria"), [ABN AMRO](/wiki/ABN_AMRO "ABN AMRO"), [Citibank](/wiki/Citibank "Citibank"), among others). There are also a myriad of brokers and financial-services bureaus, among them Ficus Capital, Galfin Sociedad de Bolsa, Europa Sociedad de Bolsa, Darío Cukier, GBU, Hordeñana \& Asociados Sociedad de Bolsa, etc.{#cite_ref-173}  

### Tourism {#Tourism}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit&section=45 "Edit section: Tourism")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Montevideo_Twilight_%28249949860%29.jpg/226px-Montevideo_Twilight_%28249949860%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Montevideo_Twilight_(249949860).jpg) Montevideo's beach on the River Plate. [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Hotel_Casino_Carrasco_%28141187153%29.jpeg/220px-Hotel_Casino_Carrasco_%28141187153%29.jpeg)](/wiki/File:Hotel_Casino_Carrasco_(141187153).jpeg) [Hotel Casino Carrasco](/wiki/Hotel_Carrasco "Hotel Carrasco")

Tourism accounts for much of Uruguay's economy. Tourism in Montevideo is centered in the Ciudad Vieja area, which includes the city's oldest buildings, several museums, art galleries, and nightclubs, with [Sarandí Street](/wiki/Peatonal_Sarand%C3%AD "Peatonal Sarandí") and the Mercado del Puerto being the most frequented venues of the old city.^[\[174\]](#cite_note-174)^ On the edge of Ciudad Vieja, [Plaza Independencia](/wiki/Plaza_Independencia "Plaza Independencia") is surrounded by many sights, including the [Solís Theatre](/wiki/Sol%C3%ADs_Theatre "Solís Theatre") and the [Palacio Salvo](/wiki/Palacio_Salvo "Palacio Salvo"); the plaza also constitutes one end of [18 de Julio Avenue](/wiki/18_de_Julio_Avenue "18 de Julio Avenue"), the city's most important tourist destination outside of Ciudad Vieja. Apart from being a shopping street, the avenue is noted for its [Art Deco](/wiki/Art_Deco "Art Deco") buildings,^[\[175\]](#cite_note-175)^ three important public squares, the Gaucho Museum, the [Palacio Municipal](/wiki/Palacio_Municipal_(Montevideo) "Palacio Municipal (Montevideo)") and many other sights. The avenue leads to the [Obelisk of Montevideo](/wiki/Obelisk_of_Montevideo "Obelisk of Montevideo"); beyond that is [Parque Batlle](/wiki/Parque_Batlle "Parque Batlle"), which along with the [Parque Prado](/wiki/Parque_Prado "Parque Prado") is another important tourist destination.^[\[176\]](#cite_note-176)^ Along the coast, the [Fortaleza del Cerro](/wiki/Fortaleza_del_Cerro "Fortaleza del Cerro"), the [*Rambla*](/wiki/La_Rambla,_Montevideo "La Rambla, Montevideo") (the coastal avenue), 13 kilometers (8.1 mi) of sandy beaches,^[\[177\]](#cite_note-177)^ and [Punta Gorda](/wiki/Punta_Gorda,_Montevideo "Punta Gorda, Montevideo") attract many tourists, as do the [Barrio Sur](/wiki/Barrio_Sur,_Montevideo "Barrio Sur, Montevideo") and [Palermo](/wiki/Palermo,_Montevideo "Palermo, Montevideo") *barrios* .^[\[178\]](#cite_note-178)^{#cite_ref-178}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Avenida_18_de_Julio_Montevideo%2C_Uruguay_2021.jpg/225px-Avenida_18_de_Julio_Montevideo%2C_Uruguay_2021.jpg)](/wiki/File:Avenida_18_de_Julio_Montevideo,_Uruguay_2021.jpg) [18 de Julio Avenue](/wiki/18_de_Julio_Avenue "18 de Julio Avenue")

The [Ministry of Tourism](/wiki/Ministry_of_Tourism_(Uruguay) "Ministry of Tourism (Uruguay)") offers a two-and-a-half-hour city tour^[\[179\]](#cite_note-179)^ and the Montevideo Tourist Guide Association offers guided tours in English, Italian, Portuguese and German.^[\[180\]](#cite_note-180)^ Apart from these, many private companies offer organized city tours.{#cite_ref-180}

Most tourists to the city come from Argentina, Brazil and Europe, with the number of visitors from elsewhere in Latin America and from the United States growing every year, thanks to an increasing number of international airline arrivals at [Carrasco International Airport](/wiki/Carrasco_International_Airport "Carrasco International Airport") as well as cruises and ferries that arrive into the port of Montevideo.  

### Retail {#Retail}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit&section=46 "Edit section: Retail")\]

Montevideo is the heartland of retailing in Uruguay. The city has become the principal center of business and real estate, including many expensive buildings and modern towers for residences and offices, surrounded by extensive green spaces. In 1985, the first shopping center in Rio de la Plata, [Montevideo Shopping](/wiki/Montevideo_Shopping "Montevideo Shopping") was built.^[\[181\]](#cite_note-181)^ In 1994, with the building of three more shopping complexes such as the [Shopping Tres Cruces](/wiki/Tres_Cruces_bus_station "Tres Cruces bus station"), [Portones Shopping](/wiki/Portones_Shopping "Portones Shopping"), and [Punta Carretas Shopping](/wiki/Punta_Carretas_Shopping "Punta Carretas Shopping"), the business map of the city changed dramatically. The creation of shopping complexes brought a major change in the habits of the people of Montevideo. Global firms such as [McDonald's](/wiki/McDonald%27s "McDonald's") and [Burger King](/wiki/Burger_King "Burger King") etc. are firmly established in Montevideo. In 2013 [Nuevocentro Shopping](/wiki/Nuevocentro_Shopping "Nuevocentro Shopping"), a shopping mall located in the [Jacinto Vera](/wiki/Jacinto_Vera,_Montevideo "Jacinto Vera, Montevideo") neighborhood, was inaugurated.^[\[182\]](#cite_note-182)^{#cite_ref-182}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Portones_Shopping_Estacionamiento.png/224px-Portones_Shopping_Estacionamiento.png)](/wiki/File:Portones_Shopping_Estacionamiento.png) Portones shopping center.

Apart from the big shopping complexes, the main retailing venues of the city are: most of 18 de Julio Avenue in the [Centro](/wiki/Centro,_Montevideo "Centro, Montevideo") and [Cordón](/wiki/Cord%C3%B3n "Cordón") *barrios* , a length of Agraciada Avenue in the Paso de Molino area of [Belvedere](/wiki/Belvedere,_Montevideo "Belvedere, Montevideo"), a length of Arenal Grande St. and the  

### Media {#Media}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit&section=47 "Edit section: Media")\]

Out of the 100 radio stations found in Uruguay, 40 of them are in Montevideo. The city has a vibrant artistic and literary community. The press enjoyed full freedom until the advent of the [Civic-military dictatorship (1973--1985)](/wiki/Civic-military_dictatorship_of_Uruguay "Civic-military dictatorship of Uruguay"); this freedom returned on 1 March 1985, as part of the restoration of democracy.

Some of the important newspapers published in the city are: *[Brecha](/wiki/Brecha_(newspaper) "Brecha (newspaper)")* , *[La República](/wiki/La_Rep%C3%BAblica_(Uruguay) "La República (Uruguay)")* , *[El Observador](/wiki/El_Observador_(Uruguay) "El Observador (Uruguay)")* ,^[\[183\]](#cite_note-183)^ *[El País](/wiki/El_Pa%C3%ADs_(Uruguay) "El País (Uruguay)")* , *Gaceta Comercial* and *La Diaria* .^[\[184\]](#cite_note-Crowther-184)^ *[El Día](/wiki/El_D%C3%ADa_(Uruguay) "El Día (Uruguay)")* was the most prestigious paper in Uruguay, founded in 1886 by José Batlle, who would later go on to become President of Uruguay. The paper ceased production in the early 1990s.^[\[185\]](#cite_note-185)^ All television stations have their headquarters in Montevideo, for example: [Saeta Channel 10](/wiki/Channel_10_(Uruguay) "Channel 10 (Uruguay)"), [Teledoce](/wiki/Teledoce "Teledoce"), [Channel 4](/wiki/Channel_4,_Uruguay "Channel 4, Uruguay") and [National Television (Channel 5)](/wiki/Televisi%C3%B3n_Nacional_Uruguay "Televisión Nacional Uruguay"){#cite_ref-185}  

Transport {#Transport}
----------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit&section=48 "Edit section: Transport")\]  

### Public transport {#Public_transport}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit&section=49 "Edit section: Public transport")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Bus_CUTCSA_de_Montevideo%2C_Uruguay.png/230px-Bus_CUTCSA_de_Montevideo%2C_Uruguay.png)](/wiki/File:Bus_CUTCSA_de_Montevideo,_Uruguay.png) Bus of CUTCSA, the largest bus company in Montevideo.

The city and its [metropolitan area](/wiki/Montevideo_metropolitan_area "Montevideo metropolitan area") have a bus transportation network, the *Sistema Met* s acronym. It covers urban and interurban services within the Metropolitan Area and is administered by the municipal government together with the [Ministry of Transport and Public Works](/wiki/Ministry_of_Transport_and_Public_Works_(Uruguay) "Ministry of Transport and Public Works (Uruguay)"). The Baltasar Brum Terminal located in [Ciudad Vieja](/wiki/Ciudad_Vieja,_Montevideo "Ciudad Vieja, Montevideo"), is the main urban bus station.^[\[186\]](#cite_note-186)^ However, there are numerous interchanges and terminals distributed in both the city and the metropolitan area.{#cite_ref-186}  

### Taxis {#Taxis}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit&section=50 "Edit section: Taxis")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Taxis_de_Montevideo%2C_Uruguay._542.jpg/229px-Taxis_de_Montevideo%2C_Uruguay._542.jpg)](/wiki/File:Taxis_de_Montevideo,_Uruguay._542.jpg) Taxis of Montevideo.

The livery of most Montevideo taxis features white on the sides, along with a yellow band, as well as yellow on the top of the car. To determine the rate they use a taximeter, which will determine the price depending on the distance traveled. All taxis accept cash, although it is also common that a passenger can pay with a credit card.^[\[187\]](#cite_note-187)^{#cite_ref-187}  

### Rail {#Rail}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit&section=51 "Edit section: Rail")\]

The [State Railways Administration of Uruguay](/wiki/State_Railways_Administration_of_Uruguay "State Railways Administration of Uruguay") (AFE) operates three commuter rail lines, namely the Empalme Olmos, San Jose and Florida. These lines operate to major suburban areas of [Canelones](/wiki/Canelones_Department "Canelones Department"), [San José](/wiki/San_Jos%C3%A9_Department "San José Department") and [Florida](/wiki/Florida_Department "Florida Department"). Within the Montevideo city limits, local trains stop at [Lorenzo Carnelli](/wiki/Lorenzo_Carnelli "Lorenzo Carnelli"), Yatai (Step Mill), [Sayago](/wiki/Sayago,_Montevideo "Sayago, Montevideo"), Colón (line to San Jose and Florida), [Peñarol](/wiki/Pe%C3%B1arol "Peñarol") and [Manga](/wiki/Manga,_Montevideo "Manga, Montevideo") (line Empalme Olmos) stations. The historic 19th century [General Artigas Central Station](/wiki/Estaci%C3%B3n_Central_General_Artigas "Estación Central General Artigas") located in the *[barrio](/wiki/Barrio "Barrio")* [Aguada](/wiki/Aguada,_Montevideo "Aguada, Montevideo"), six blocks from the central business district, was abandoned 1 March 2003 and remains closed.^[\[188\]](#cite_note-188)^^[\[189\]](#cite_note-189)^ A new station, 500 meters (1,600 ft) north of the old one and part of the [Telecommunications Tower](/wiki/Telecommunications_Tower_(Montevideo) "Telecommunications Tower (Montevideo)") modern complex, has taken over the rail traffic.^[\[190\]](#cite_note-190)^{#cite_ref-190}

The train service is currently suspended for works related to the modernization of the railway system until mid-2023 when the work will end.^[\[13\]](#cite_note-:0-13)^^[\[23\]](#cite_note-:1-23)^^\[*[needs update](/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items "Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers")*\]^{#cite_ref-:1_23-1}  

### Intercity buses {#Intercity_buses}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit&section=52 "Edit section: Intercity buses")\]

The [Tres Cruces bus station](/wiki/Tres_Cruces_bus_station "Tres Cruces bus station") is the main bus terminal in Uruguay, serving long-distance buses that travel into Montevideo, from other parts of the country and abroad. Inaugurated in 1994, it serves more than 12 million passengers per year.^[\[191\]](#cite_note-191)^^[\[192\]](#cite_note-192)^{#cite_ref-192}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Aeropuerto_carrasco.jpg/232px-Aeropuerto_carrasco.jpg)](/wiki/File:Aeropuerto_carrasco.jpg) [Carrasco International Airport](/wiki/Carrasco_International_Airport "Carrasco International Airport")

Companies operating at Tres Cruces bus station: Agencia central, Bruno, Copsa, Cromin, Cynsa, Copay, Cot, Cut, Corporacion, Cita, Cauvi, Colonia Express, El Condor, El Norteño, Ega, Expreso Chago, Expreso Minuano, Intertur, Nossar, Nuñez, Rutas del sol, TTL, Turil, Turismar, etc.  

### Aviation {#Aviation}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit&section=53 "Edit section: Aviation")\]

Montevideo is served by the [Carrasco International Airport](/wiki/Carrasco_International_Airport "Carrasco International Airport") ([IATA](/wiki/IATA_airport_code "IATA airport code"): **MVD** , [ICAO](/wiki/ICAO_airport_code "ICAO airport code"): **SUMU** ), which is located in the north of [Ciudad de la Costa](/wiki/Ciudad_de_la_Costa "Ciudad de la Costa"), in [Canelones Department](/wiki/Canelones_Department "Canelones Department"), 19 km (12 mi) from the city center. It handles over 1,5 million passengers per year,^[\[193\]](#cite_note-Blore-193)^^[\[194\]](#cite_note-194)^ and has been cited as one of the most efficient and traveler-friendly airports in Latin America.^[\[195\]](#cite_note-195)^{#cite_ref-195}

[Ángel S. Adami Airport](/wiki/%C3%81ngel_S._Adami_Airport "Ángel S. Adami Airport") is a private airport operated by minor charter companies and in which there is also a flight school.^[\[196\]](#cite_note-196)^{#cite_ref-196}  

### Port {#Port}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit&section=54 "Edit section: Port")\]  
Main article: [Port of Montevideo](/wiki/Port_of_Montevideo "Port of Montevideo")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Colonia_del_Sacramento_2016_042.jpg/230px-Colonia_del_Sacramento_2016_042.jpg)](/wiki/File:Colonia_del_Sacramento_2016_042.jpg) [Buquebus](/wiki/Buquebus "Buquebus") high-speed ferries connect Montevideo to [Argentina](/wiki/Argentina "Argentina")

Montevideo is also served by a [ferry system](/wiki/Ferry "Ferry") operated by the company [Buquebus](/wiki/Buquebus "Buquebus") that connects the port with [Buenos Aires](/wiki/Buenos_Aires "Buenos Aires"). More than 2.2 million people per year travel between Argentina and Uruguay with Buquebus. One of these ships is a [catamaran](/wiki/Catamaran "Catamaran"), which can reach a top speed of about 80 km/h (50 mph).^[\[197\]](#cite_note-197)^{#cite_ref-197}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Stk_1340.jpg/226px-Stk_1340.jpg)](/wiki/File:Stk_1340.jpg) Port of Montevideo

The port on Montevideo Bay is one of the reasons the city was founded. It gives natural protection to ships, although two jetties now further protect the harbor entrance from waves. This natural port is competitive with the other great port of Río de la Plata, Buenos Aires.^[\[198\]](#cite_note-198)^{#cite_ref-198}

The main engineering work on the port occurred between the years 1870 and 1930. These six decades saw the construction of the port's first wooden pier, several warehouses in La Aguada, the north and south Rambla, a river port, a new pier, the dredged river basin and the [La Teja Refinery](/wiki/La_Teja_Refinery "La Teja Refinery"). A major storm in 1923 necessitated repairs to many of the city's engineering works.^[\[48\]](#cite_note-PieGau-48)^ Since the second half of the 20th century, until the 21st century, physical changes had ceased, and since that time the area had degraded due to national economic stagnation.^[\[48\]](#cite_note-PieGau-48)^{#cite_ref-PieGau_48-2}

The port's proximity has contributed to the installation of various industries in the area surrounding the bay, particularly import/export businesses and other business related to port and naval activity. The density of industrial development in the area surrounding the port has kept its popularity as a residential area relatively low despite its centrality. The main environmental problems are subaquatic sedimentation and air and water contamination.^[\[48\]](#cite_note-PieGau-48)^{#cite_ref-PieGau_48-3}

Every year more than one hundred cruises arrive, bringing tourists to Montevideo by public or private tours.^[\[199\]](#cite_note-199)^{#cite_ref-199}  

### Cycling {#Cycling}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit&section=55 "Edit section: Cycling")\]

The city has bicycle circuits in [Ciudad Vieja](/wiki/Ciudad_Vieja,_Montevideo "Ciudad Vieja, Montevideo"), [Artigas Boulevard](/wiki/Artigas_Boulevard "Artigas Boulevard") and [Centro](/wiki/Centro,_Montevideo "Centro, Montevideo") as well as with good facilities for cyclists such as bike paths and [bike racks](/wiki/Bicycle_stand "Bicycle stand") throughout the city.^[\[200\]](#cite_note-200)^ In 2013 the "South Bicicircuito" was also inaugurated, which connects several of the dependent faculties of the University of the Republic.^[\[201\]](#cite_note-201)^ There are more than 100 bike stations in the city.^[\[202\]](#cite_note-202)^ In 2014, a [bicycle sharing system](/wiki/Bicycle-sharing_system "Bicycle-sharing system") called *Movete* was launched.^[\[203\]](#cite_note-203)^{#cite_ref-203}  

Education {#Education}
----------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit&section=56 "Edit section: Education")\]  

### Public education {#Public_education}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit&section=57 "Edit section: Public education")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/2016_Facultad_de_Derecho_de_la_Universidad_de_la_Rep%C3%BAblica%2C_Avenida_18_de_Julio.jpg/234px-2016_Facultad_de_Derecho_de_la_Universidad_de_la_Rep%C3%BAblica%2C_Avenida_18_de_Julio.jpg)](/wiki/File:2016_Facultad_de_Derecho_de_la_Universidad_de_la_Rep%C3%BAblica,_Avenida_18_de_Julio.jpg) University of the Republic law school.

The [University of the Republic](/wiki/University_of_the_Republic_(Uruguay) "University of the Republic (Uruguay)") is the country's largest and most important university, with a student body of 81,774, according to the census of 2007.^[\[204\]](#cite_note-204)^ It was founded on 18 July 1849 in Montevideo, where most of its buildings and facilities are still located. Its [Rector](/wiki/Rector_(academia) "Rector (academia)") is Dr. [Rodrigo Arocena](/wiki/Rodrigo_Arocena "Rodrigo Arocena"). The university houses 14 faculties (departments) and various institutes and schools. Many eminent Uruguayans have graduated from this university, including [Carlos Vaz Ferreira](/wiki/Carlos_Vaz_Ferreira "Carlos Vaz Ferreira"), [José Luis Massera](/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Massera "José Luis Massera"), [Gabriel Paternain](/wiki/Gabriel_Paternain "Gabriel Paternain"), [Mario Wschebor](/wiki/Mario_Wschebor "Mario Wschebor"), [Roman Fresnedo Siri](/wiki/Roman_Fresnedo_Siri "Roman Fresnedo Siri"), [Carlos Ott](/wiki/Carlos_Ott "Carlos Ott") and [Eladio Dieste](/wiki/Eladio_Dieste "Eladio Dieste"){#cite_ref-204}

The process of founding the country's public university began on 11 June 1833 with the passage of a law proposed by Senator Dámaso Antonio Larrañaga. It called for the creation of nine academic departments; the President of the Republic would pass a decree formally creating the departments once the majority of them were in operation. In 1836, the House of General Studies was formed, housing the departments of Latin, philosophy, mathematics, theology and jurisprudence. On 27 May 1838, [Manuel Oribe](/wiki/Manuel_Oribe "Manuel Oribe") passed a decree establishing the Greater University of the Republic.^[\[205\]](#cite_note-205)^ That decree had few practical effects, given the institutional instability of the Oriental Republic of Uruguay at that time.{#cite_ref-205}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Kindergarten_kids_at_a_public_school_in_Montevideo%2C_Uruguay.jpg/220px-Kindergarten_kids_at_a_public_school_in_Montevideo%2C_Uruguay.jpg)](/wiki/File:Kindergarten_kids_at_a_public_school_in_Montevideo,_Uruguay.jpg) Kindergarten kids at a public school in Montevideo  

### Private education {#Private_education}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit&section=58 "Edit section: Private education")\]

The largest private university in Uruguay,^[\[206\]](#cite_note-206)^ is also located in Montevideo. [ORT Uruguay](/wiki/Universidad_ORT_Uruguay "Universidad ORT Uruguay") was first established as a non-profit organization in 1942, and was officially certified as a private university in September 1996, becoming the second private educational institution in the country to achieve that status.^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^ It is a member of [World ORT](/wiki/World_ORT "World ORT"), an international educational network founded in 1880 by the Jewish community in [Saint Petersburg](/wiki/Saint_Petersburg "Saint Petersburg"), Russia.^[\[207\]](#cite_note-207)^ The university has about 8,000 students, distributed among 5 faculties and institutes, mainly geared towards the sciences and technology/engineering. Its rector as of 2010^[\[update\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit)^ is Dr. Jorge A. Grünberg.{#cite_ref-207}

Another private university in Uruguay is the [University of Montevideo](/wiki/University_of_Montevideo "University of Montevideo") (Spanish: Universidad de Montevideo, short: UM). It opened in 1986 and obtained the right to be legally named a [university](/wiki/University "University") in 1997. With its seven schools the UM has facilities all over Montevideo. The Universidad de Montevideo also holds more than 250 partnerships with other universities in 47 countries. Since 2019 is the university ranked in the Top 500 in the world by the [QS World University Rankings](/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings "QS World University Rankings") (QSWUR). ^[\[208\]](#cite_note-208)^{#cite_ref-208}

The Montevideo [Crandon Institute](/wiki/Crandon_Institute "Crandon Institute") is an American School of missionary origin and the main [Methodist](/wiki/Methodist_Church "Methodist Church") educational institution in Uruguay. Founded in 1879 and supported by the Women's Society of the Methodist Church of the United States, it is one of the most traditional and emblematic institutions in the city inculcating [John Wesley](/wiki/John_Wesley "John Wesley")'s values. Its alumni include presidents, senators, ambassadors and Nobel Prize winners^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^, along with musicians, scientists, and others. The Montevideo Crandon Institute boasts of being the first academic institution in South America where a [home economics](/wiki/Home_economics "Home economics") course was taught.^[\[209\]](#cite_note-209)^^[\[210\]](#cite_note-210)^{#cite_ref-210}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Montevideo_school_play_laundress.jpg/170px-Montevideo_school_play_laundress.jpg)](/wiki/File:Montevideo_school_play_laundress.jpg) A laundress girl in a school play in Montevideo

The [Christian Brothers of Ireland](/wiki/Christian_Brothers_of_Ireland "Christian Brothers of Ireland") [Stella Maris College](/wiki/Stella_Maris_College_(Montevideo) "Stella Maris College (Montevideo)") is a private, [co-educational](/wiki/Co-educational "Co-educational"), [not-for-profit](/wiki/Not-for-profit "Not-for-profit") Catholic school located in the wealthy residential southeastern neighborhood of [Carrasco](/wiki/Carrasco,_Montevideo "Carrasco, Montevideo"). Established in 1955, it is regarded as one of the best high schools in the country, blending a rigorous curriculum with strong extracurricular activities.^[\[211\]](#cite_note-211)^ The school's headmaster, history professor Juan Pedro Toni, is a member of the Stella Maris Board of Governors and the school is a member of the [International Baccalaureate Organization](/wiki/International_Baccalaureate_Organization "International Baccalaureate Organization") (IBO). Its long list of distinguished former pupils includes economists, engineers, architects, lawyers, politicians and even [F1](/wiki/Formula_One "Formula One") champions. The school has also played an important part in the development of [rugby union in Uruguay](/wiki/Rugby_union_in_Uruguay "Rugby union in Uruguay"), with the creation of [Old Christians Club](/wiki/Old_Christians_Club "Old Christians Club"), the school's [alumni](/wiki/Alumnus "Alumnus") club.{#cite_ref-211}

Also in Carrasco is [The British Schools of Montevideo](/wiki/The_British_Schools_of_Montevideo "The British Schools of Montevideo"), one of the oldest educational institutions in the country, founded in 1908 with "the object of giving children a complete education, both intellectual and moral, based upon the ideas and principles of the best schools in The British Isles".^[\[212\]](#cite_note-212)^ The School is governed by the Board of Governors, elected by the British Schools Society in Uruguay, whose honorary president is the British Ambassador to Uruguay. Prominent alumni include president [Luis Lacalle Pou](/wiki/Luis_Lacalle_Pou "Luis Lacalle Pou") and former government ministers [Pedro Bordaberry](/wiki/Pedro_Bordaberry "Pedro Bordaberry") and [Gabriel Gurméndez Armand-Ugon](/wiki/Gabriel_Gurm%C3%A9ndez_Armand-Ugon "Gabriel Gurméndez Armand-Ugon").{#cite_ref-212}

Located in Cordon, St.Brendan's school, previously named St.Catherine's is a non-profit civil association, which has a solid institutional culture with a clear vision of the future. It is known for being one of the best schools in the country, joining students from the wealthiest parts of Montevideo, such as, Punta Carretas, Pocitos, Malvin and Carrasco. St. Brendan's School is a bilingual, non-denominational school that promotes a pedagogical constructivist approach focused on the child as a whole. In this approach, understanding is built from the connections children make between their own prior knowledge and the learning experiences, thus developing critical thinking skills. It is also the only school in the country implementing the three [International Baccalaureate Programmes](/wiki/International_Baccalaureate_Programme "International Baccalaureate Programme"). These are:

* Diploma Program -- Pre-University course for students aged 16 to 19. The Diploma Program is a two-year curriculum.
* MYP -Middle Years Program. For students aged 12 to 16.
* PYP -- Primary Years Program. For students aged 3 to 12.

Other educational institutions of note include Colegio Ingles, [John XXIII Institute](/wiki/John_XXIII_Institute "John XXIII Institute"), [Lycée Français de Montevideo](/wiki/Lyc%C3%A9e_Fran%C3%A7ais_de_Montevideo "Lycée Français de Montevideo"), Ivy Thomas, [German School of Montevideo](/wiki/German_School_of_Montevideo "German School of Montevideo") and Colegio Preuniversitario Ciudad de San Felipe.^[\[213\]](#cite_note-213)^{#cite_ref-213}  

Healthcare {#Healthcare}
------------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit&section=59 "Edit section: Healthcare")\]  
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Hospital_italiano_de_Montevideo.jpg/205px-Hospital_italiano_de_Montevideo.jpg)](/wiki/File:Hospital_italiano_de_Montevideo.jpg)  
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Hospital_de_Clinicas_-_panoramio.jpg/180px-Hospital_de_Clinicas_-_panoramio.jpg)](/wiki/File:Hospital_de_Clinicas_-_panoramio.jpg)  
Left: [Italian Hospital of Montevideo](/wiki/Italian_Hospital_of_Montevideo "Italian Hospital of Montevideo"). Right: [Hospital Clinic](/wiki/Hospital_Clinic_Manuel_Quintela "Hospital Clinic Manuel Quintela")

In Montevideo, as elsewhere in the country, there are both public and private health services. In both sectors, medical services are provided by [polyclinics](/wiki/Polyclinic "Polyclinic") and hospitals or sanatorios. The term *hospital* is used here for both outpatient and inpatient facilities, while *sanatorio* is used for private short- and long-term facilities for the treatment of illnesses.  

### Public hospitals {#Public_hospitals}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit&section=60 "Edit section: Public hospitals")\]

[Hospital de Clínicas "Dr. Manuel Quintela"](/wiki/Manuel_Quintela_Clinic_Hospital "Manuel Quintela Clinic Hospital") is a University Hospital attached to the [University of the Republic](/wiki/University_of_the_Republic "University of the Republic"), and is located on [Avenida Italia](/wiki/Avenida_Italia "Avenida Italia"). It functions as an adult general polyclinic and hospital. The building was designed by architect Carlos Surraco in 1928--1929 and has a surface area of 110,000 square meters (1,200,000 sq ft) on 23 floors. The hospital was inaugurated 21 September 1953. For many years it was led by Dr. [Hugo Villar](/wiki/Hugo_Villar "Hugo Villar"), who was a considerable influence on the institution.

[Hospital Maciel](/wiki/Hospital_Maciel "Hospital Maciel") is one of the oldest hospitals in Uruguay and stands on the block bounded by the streets Maciel, 25 de Mayo, Guaraní and Washington, with the main entrance at 25 de Mayo, 172. The land was originally donated in Spanish colonial times by philanthropist [Francisco Antonio Maciel](/wiki/Francisco_Antonio_Maciel "Francisco Antonio Maciel"), who teamed up with [Mateo Vidal](/wiki/Mateo_Vidal "Mateo Vidal") to establish a hospital and charity. The first building was constructed between 1781 and 1788 and later expanded upon. The present building stems from the 1825 plans of José Toribio (son of [Tomás Toribio](/w/index.php?title=Tom%C3%A1s_Toribio&action=edit&redlink=1 "Tomás Toribio (page does not exist)") \[[es](https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tom%C3%A1s_Toribio "es:Tomás Toribio")\]) and later [Bernardo Poncini](/wiki/Bernardo_Poncini "Bernardo Poncini") (wing on the Guaraní street, 1859), Eduardo Canstatt (corner of Guaraní and 25 de Mayo) and Julián Masquelez (1889).^[\[214\]](#cite_note-214)^ The hospital has a [chapel built in Greek style](/wiki/Capilla_de_la_Caridad_del_Hospital_Maciel,_Montevideo "Capilla de la Caridad del Hospital Maciel, Montevideo") by Miguel Estévez in 1798.^[\[215\]](#cite_note-215)^{#cite_ref-215}

[Hospital Pereira Rossell](/wiki/Hospital_Pereira_Rossell "Hospital Pereira Rossell") was founded in 1908 and was built on land donated in late 1900 by Alexis Rossell y Rius and Dolores Pereira de Rossell.^[\[216\]](#cite_note-216)^ It was the city's first pediatric hospital, and shortly afterwards the addition of an obstetric and gynecological clinic in 1915 made it the first maternity hospital as well. Later, the hospital received a donation from Dr. Enrique Pouey for a radiotherapy unit.{#cite_ref-216}

[Hospital Vilardebó](/wiki/Hospital_Vilardeb%C3%B3 "Hospital Vilardebó") is the only psychiatric hospital in Montevideo. Named after the physician and naturalist [Teodoro Vilardebó](/w/index.php?title=Teodoro_Vilardeb%C3%B3&action=edit&redlink=1 "Teodoro Vilardebó (page does not exist)") \[[es](https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Teodoro_Vilardeb%C3%B3_Matuliche "es:Teodoro Vilardebó Matuliche")\], it opened 21 May 1880.^[\[217\]](#cite_note-217)^ The hospital was originally one of the best of Latin America and in 1915 grew to 1,500 inpatients. Today the hospital is very deteriorated, with broken walls and floors, lack of medicines, beds, and rooms for the personnel.^[\[218\]](#cite_note-218)^ It has an emergency service, outpatient, clinic and inpatient rooms and employs approximately 610 staff, psychologists, psychiatrists, social workers, administrators, guards, among others.^[\[219\]](#cite_note-219)^ The average patient age is 30 years; more than half of the patients arrive by court order; 42% suffer from schizophrenia, 18% from depression and mania,^[\[220\]](#cite_note-220)^ and there are also a high percentage of drug addicted patients.{#cite_ref-220}

Other public polyclinics and hospitals of note include the [Hospital Saint Bois](/wiki/Hospital_Saint_Bois "Hospital Saint Bois"), founded 18 November 1928, which consists of a General Hospital and Eye Hospital; the Pasteur Hospital in La Unión neighborhood; the [Hospital Español](/wiki/Spanish_Hospital_(Uruguay) "Spanish Hospital (Uruguay)"), which was founded in 1886, passed to the private sector in the 20th century, closed in 2004 and was restored and re-inaugurated in 2007 as the municipal Juan Jose Crottogini Polyclinic;^[\[221\]](#cite_note-221)^^[\[222\]](#cite_note-222)^ the National Cancer Institute; and the National Institute of Trauma and Orthopedics.{#cite_ref-222}  

### Private healthcare {#Private_healthcare}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Montevideo&action=edit&section=61 "Edit section: Private healthcare")\]

Private healthcare is offered by many private health insurance companies, each of which has one or more polyclinics and owns or is associated with one or more hospitals. Private medical facilities of note include the [Hospital Británico](/wiki/Hospital_Brit%C3%A1nico_(Montevideo) "Hospital Británico (Montevideo)"), the [Italian Hospital of Montevideo](/wiki/Italian_Hospital_of_Montevideo "Italian Hospital of Montevideo"), Mutualista CASMU's Sanatoria I, II, III and IV, the Evangelical Hospital, [Médica Uruguaya](/w/index.php?title=M%C3%A9dica_Uruguaya&action=edit&redlink=1 "Médica Uruguaya (page does not exist)") \[[es](https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/M%C3%A9dica_Uruguaya "es:Médica Uruguaya")\], Sanatorio de la Asociación Española, Sanatorios del Círculo Católico, Sanatorio Casa de Galicia and Sanatorio GREMCA.

Pocas villas con deseos de ser ciudad, tuvieron tantos prenombres hasta llegar al definitivo de Montevideo. Pináculo de la Tentación, Monte de la Detención, Nuestra Señora de la Candelaria, Monte de San Pedro, Santo Vidio, Monte Seredo, Monte Vidi, Monte veo, Montem Video, Monte Vide Eu, Monte Ovidio, Monte VI D. E-O... Tales fueron, entre el viaje de Amerigo Vespucci (1501) y la fundación por Bruno Mauricio de Zabala (1726), las diversas denominaciones que la elevación al oeste de la bahía recibió.{#cite_note-27}

* Finzer, R David. [*The Southron's Guide to Living in Uruguay*](https://books.google.com/books?id=Z9Up1rOz8mQC&pg=PA98). The Southron. [ISBN](/wiki/ISBN_(identifier) "ISBN (identifier)") [982-9801-31-4](/wiki/Special:BookSources/982-9801-31-4 "Special:BookSources/982-9801-31-4").
